# Kerf — Roadmap

**Status glyphs:** `✅ shipped` · `🚧 in flight` · `🔴 not started`

---

## North Star

**The most comprehensive CAD on Earth — a single tool in which a person can design *anything*.** Mechanical engineering, electronics, PCB, architecture, civil engineering, drafting, jewelry, automotive — and every other CAD sector, including the small and niche ones. We are doing **everything**. Nothing here is "cut." Lower priority means *later*, not *dropped*.

This is a **priority-ordered** roadmap, not a date-ordered or effort-ordered one. The tiers (P0 → P3) express sequence and leverage: which items earn the most credibility per unit of work.

Kerf is dual-licensed: the OSS core (MIT) and the hosted-tier code under `packages/kerf-{billing,cloud}/` + `src/cloud/`.

### Why chat-driven CAD works

Kerf is **chat-driven** CAD. Every capability is designed around one constraint:

> *Can the LLM produce and re-edit this deliverable through a text-native tool, and verify the result?*

Professional CAD is overcomplicated mostly because of command-discovery affordances (ribbons, palettes, wizards) that an LLM does not need. Kerf ships professional **capability** while deliberately not shipping professional **UI complexity**. This makes the roadmap shorter than it looks: many "pro features" are UX wrappers around a parametric core we expose as a text schema + LLM tool + verifier.

**Hard guardrail:** simplification is about *authoring mechanics only*. It is never an excuse to drop a domain or to skimp on correctness, output formats, or standards compliance. Those are *more* important under an LLM, not less.

---

## Platform foundation

The sector work only matters if you **own your work, are not locked in, and can run Kerf wherever you want**. Four commitments, all decided:

1. **Every cloud project is a real git repository** — `git clone`-able with stock git, no special client. Large or binary files are auto-detected and stored with a small in-git pointer. Version control is two complementary layers: fine-grained automatic file history *and* deliberate, shareable commits with GitHub sync.

2. **One client, cloud by default, easy optional self-host** — `pip install kerf` for the hosted cloud; `pip install 'kerf[server]'` + bring-your-own-Postgres + `kerf serve` for self-host. Same client, same data model, both paths first-class.

3. **Portability is the anti-lock-in guarantee** — `kerf sync` mirrors to a local folder with two-way sync; `kerf export` / `kerf import` produce and ingest a plain file tree. Moving a project between cloud and self-host is painless.

4. **A fully-local / offline desktop app is committed but demand-gated** — portability + two-way sync + easy self-host is the complete launch answer to "I want to own my data." The standalone offline desktop build is sequenced behind real demand.

---

## What shipped

### Latest delta — 2026-05-31

**ELEC-ZENER-CLAMP** ✅ — Zener-diode voltage clamp + series resistor design for DC supply rail regulation. `design_zener_clamp(ZenerClampSpec) -> ZenerClampReport` in `kerf_electronics.zener_clamp_design`. Dataclasses: `ZenerClampSpec` (V_in_min_V, V_in_max_V, V_zener_V, I_load_min_A, I_load_max_A, V_zener_tolerance_pct=5.0, I_zener_knee_A=0.001); `ZenerClampReport` (R_series_ohm, R_series_power_W, I_zener_max_A, P_zener_max_W, recommended_zener_package, recommended_R_E12_ohm, regulation_pct, honest_caveat). Algorithm: R = (V_in_max − V_Z) / (I_load_min + I_knee); V_Z_max = V_Z×(1+tol/100); I_Z_max = (V_in_max − V_Z_max)/R − I_load_min; P_Z_design = V_Z × I_Z_max × 1.25 (25% derating margin per Vishay AN-2014-3 §3); P_R = (V_in_max − V_Z) × (I_Z_max + I_load_min). Zener package thresholds: 0.4 W (DO-35/SOD-80, BZX55 series), 0.5 W (DO-41, BZX79), 1 W (DO-41/BZX85, 1N4728–1N4764), 3 W (DO-201/P600), 5 W (SOT-89/TO-252). E12 series resistor from IEC 60063 (round up for conservative power). `electronics_design_zener_clamp` LLM tool registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_electronics/__init__.py`. 60 tests green. HONEST: SIMPLE LINEAR SHUNT REGULATOR ONLY — wasted power = (V_in_max−V_Z)×I_R_total regardless of load draw; at zero load ALL current flows through Zener; for I_load > 100 mA or efficiency-sensitive rails STRONGLY prefer LDO linear regulator (LM1117, MCP1700) or switching buck converter; Zener incremental resistance rZ NOT modelled (ΔV_out = rZ×ΔI_Z — typical rZ 7–20 Ω for 5 V / 400 mW parts — use TL431 or shunt reference IC for tight regulation); temperature coefficient of V_Z NOT modelled (below ~5 V TC is negative, above ~5.6 V positive; ≈5.1 V Zeners have ~0 TC); 25% margin is steady-state — pulse/transient peaks require JEDEC JESD51-2 transient thermal impedance analysis; static regulation = 2×tol% only (dynamic line/load from rZ excluded). Refs: Horowitz & Hill "Art of Electronics" 3e §2.2.4; Vishay Application Note AN-2014-3 — `packages/kerf-electronics/src/kerf_electronics/zener_clamp_design.py`.

**ELEC-OP-AMP-OFFSET-DRIFT** ✅ — Op-amp input offset voltage and temperature drift calculator for precision instrumentation design. `compute_op_amp_drift(OpAmpSpec, CircuitSpec, error_budget_pct=0.1) -> OpAmpOffsetReport` in `kerf_electronics.op_amp_offset_drift`. Dataclasses: `OpAmpSpec` (Vos_typ_uV, Vos_drift_uV_per_C, T_ambient_min_C, T_ambient_max_C, T_reference_C=25.0); `CircuitSpec` (gain_VV, signal_full_scale_V); `OpAmpOffsetReport` (Vos_at_T_min_uV, Vos_at_T_max_uV, Vos_max_input_referred_uV, Vos_max_output_referred_mV, error_pct_of_FS, within_spec, recommended_op_amp_class, honest_caveat). Algorithm: Vos(T) = Vos_typ + TC_Vos × (T − T_ref) (TI SLOA069 §3 Eq. 3-1); worst-case evaluates all 4 (±drift × ±endpoint) combinations and takes max absolute; Vos_max_IR = max(|Vos(T_min)|, |Vos(T_max)|); Vos_OR_mV = gain × Vos_max_IR / 1000; error_pct = 100 × (Vos_OR_mV/1000) / FS. Class thresholds: "chopper" (TC_Vos ≤ 0.05 µV/°C, e.g. AD8551, MAX420); "zero-drift" (≤ 0.1 µV/°C, e.g. OPA188, LTC2050); "precision" (≤ 1.0 µV/°C, e.g. OPA227, LT1012); "standard" (> 1.0 µV/°C). Recommendation: "chopper" when error ≥ 10× budget; "precision" when over budget; confirm class from TC when in budget. Reference design (task spec): Vos=100 µV, drift=2 µV/°C, T=[0..70]°C, gain=100, FS=5V → Vos(T_max)=190 µV, output=19 mV, error=0.38%. `electronics_compute_op_amp_drift` LLM tool registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_electronics/__init__.py`. 24 tests green. HONEST: linear drift model ONLY — Vos(T)=Vos_typ+TC_Vos×ΔT; real drift is non-linear and asymmetric (TI SLOA069 Fig 3-2); Vos_typ is nominal (not guaranteed — use Vos_max for design margin); **1/f (flicker) noise contribution to DC offset NOT modelled** (can dominate sub-Hz BJT-input amps); **PSRR/CMRR cross-talk effects OUT OF SCOPE** (ΔVos_PSRR = ΔVPS/PSRR must be added separately); resistor TC mismatch in feedback network adds gain-drift error not captured. Refs: TI "Op Amp Errors" SLOA069 §3 Eq. 3-1; Analog Devices AN-580 §1; OPA188 / AD8551 / LT1012 datasheets — `packages/kerf-electronics/src/kerf_electronics/op_amp_offset_drift.py`.

**ELEC-INDUCTOR-CORE-SAT** ✅ — Inductor core saturation checker. `check_inductor_saturation(InductorCoreSpec, InductorCurrentSpec) -> CoreSaturationReport` in `kerf_electronics.inductor_core_saturation`. Dataclasses: `InductorCoreSpec` (material: "ferrite_3C95"|"ferrite_3F36"|"powdered_iron_-26"|"sendust"|"NiFe50", A_e_mm2, l_e_mm, B_sat_mT, mu_r); `InductorCurrentSpec` (turns_N, I_dc_A, I_ripple_peak_to_peak_A, temperature_C=25.0); `CoreSaturationReport` (B_peak_mT, B_sat_mT, saturation_margin_pct, saturated, recommended_max_I_dc_A, honest_caveat). Algorithm: I_pk = I_dc + I_ripple_pp/2; B_pk = μ₀·μ_r·N·I_pk/l_e (Ampere's law, uniform closed path); saturation_margin = (B_sat − B_pk)/B_sat × 100; saturated = B_pk >= B_sat; recommended_max_I_dc = max(0, 0.99·B_sat·l_e/(μ₀·μ_r·N) − I_ripple/2). Temperature derating for ferrite materials: piecewise-linear (100°C→−15%, 125°C→−25%, 150°C→−40%, 200°C→−50%) per Ferroxcube 3C95/3F36 datasheets; not applied to powder-iron/Sendust/NiFe. `electronics_check_inductor_saturation` LLM tool registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_electronics/__init__.py`. 26 tests green. HONEST: fringing flux ignored (gapped cores need Dowell/Erickson §15.3 gap fringing correction); μ_r assumed constant (real ferrite μ_r rolls off substantially in the knee region BEFORE B_sat — model over-estimates B_pk conservatively; use nonlinear B-H curve for precision); non-ferrite B_sat derating NOT modelled; winding I²R temperature rise NOT accounted; AC core losses (Steinmetz) NOT computed — `packages/kerf-electronics/src/kerf_electronics/inductor_core_saturation.py`. Refs: Erickson "Power Electronics" 3e §15; McLyman "Transformer and Inductor Design Handbook" 4e §10; Ferroxcube 3C95/3F36 datasheets; Magnetics Inc. Powder Core Catalog §3.

**ELEC-FET-SOA-CHECK** ✅ — MOSFET Safe Operating Area (SOA) checker. `check_fet_soa(FETSpec, FETOperatingPoint) -> FETSOAReport` in `kerf_electronics.fet_soa_check`. Dataclasses: `FETSpec` (part_number, V_DSS_max_V, I_D_continuous_A, I_D_pulsed_A, R_DS_on_mOhm, T_J_max_C, R_theta_JA_K_per_W, P_D_max_W); `FETOperatingPoint` (V_DS_V, I_D_A, pulse_duration_ms, duty_cycle, T_ambient_C); `FETSOAReport` (within_soa, P_diss_W, T_junction_estimate_C, soa_violation_modes, headroom_pct, honest_caveat). Algorithm: P_diss = V_DS × I_D × duty; T_J = T_amb + P_diss × R_θJA (Jedec JESD51 single-node); violation checks: V_DSS_exceeded (V_DS > V_DSS_max), I_D_continuous_exceeded (duty==1.0 AND I_D > I_D_continuous), I_D_pulsed_exceeded (duty<1.0 AND I_D > I_D_pulsed), T_J_exceeded (T_J > T_J_max), P_D_exceeded (P_diss > P_D_max); headroom_pct = (1 − max(utilisation_ratios)) × 100. `electronics_check_fet_soa` LLM tool registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_electronics/__init__.py`. 30 tests green. HONEST: LINEARISED SOA only — real datasheet SOA curves (IRF Hexfet Designer's Manual §5 Fig 5-1) are non-linear in the thermal-limited and second-breakdown regions; pulse-width SOA NOT interpolated (short pulses allow higher peak I_D×V_DS before the thermal integral exceeds the die's transient thermal capacity); second-breakdown (avalanche/UIS) NOT explicitly modelled as a separate boundary — for inductive turn-off verify E_AS = ½·L·I_peak² < rated E_AS; thermal model is single-node JESD51 steady-state R_θJA (not transient Z_θJC(t)); R_DS_on is room-temperature datasheet value (actual R_DS_on increases with T_J per Infineon AN 2015-11); switching losses (turn-on, turn-off, gate charge) NOT included in P_diss — `packages/kerf-electronics/src/kerf_electronics/fet_soa_check.py`. Refs: IRF Hexfet Designer's Manual §5; IPC-9701A; Jedec JESD51-1; Infineon AN 2015-11.

**ELEC-LDO-DROPOUT-CHECK** ✅ — LDO linear regulator dropout and thermal compliance checker. `check_ldo_dropout(LDOSpec) -> LDODropoutReport` in `kerf_electronics.ldo_dropout_check`. Dataclasses: `LDOSpec` (V_out_V, V_in_min_V, V_in_max_V, I_load_A, dropout_voltage_at_max_load_mV, junction_to_ambient_thermal_resistance_K_per_W, T_ambient_C=25, T_max_junction_C=125); `LDODropoutReport` (headroom_min_mV, dropout_compliant, power_dissipation_W, junction_temp_estimate_C, thermal_compliant, efficiency_pct, honest_caveat). Algorithm: headroom_mV = (V_in_min − V_out) × 1000; dropout_compliant = headroom_mV > dropout_spec_mV (strict); P_diss = (V_in_max − V_out) × I_load; T_j = T_ambient + P_diss × R_θja (Jedec JESD51 single-node); thermal_compliant = T_j < T_max_junction; efficiency = 100 × V_out / V_in_max (pessimistic). `electronics_check_ldo_dropout` LLM tool registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_electronics/__init__.py`. 54 tests green. HONEST: quiescent current I_Q NOT included (dominates at light load — TI Power Ref §3.2.3); transient headroom NOT checked (PSRR roll-off + input cap droop during load steps; add ≥100–200 mV guard-band per Sandler §4.4); output capacitor stability NOT verified (ESR window requirement); thermal model is θja worst-case (θjb+θjc paths not modelled); efficiency = V_out/V_in_max ignores I_Q — `packages/kerf-electronics/src/kerf_electronics/ldo_dropout_check.py`. Refs: TI Power Reference Manual §3; Sandler "Switch-Mode Power Supplies" §4; Jedec JESD51-1.

**ELEC-DC-DC-CONVERTER-RIPPLE** ✅ — Output voltage ripple ΔV_out (peak-to-peak) for a buck DC-DC converter in Continuous Conduction Mode (CCM). `compute_buck_ripple(BuckConverterSpec) -> ConverterRippleReport` in `kerf_electronics.dc_dc_ripple`. Dataclasses: `BuckConverterSpec` (V_in_V, V_out_V, I_load_A, switching_freq_Hz, L_uH, C_out_uF, C_ESR_mOhm); `ConverterRippleReport` (delta_iL_pp_A, delta_V_out_pp_mV, delta_V_capacitor_mV, delta_V_ESR_mV, duty_cycle, output_ripple_pct, honest_caveat). Algorithm: D = V_out/V_in; ΔiL = (V_in−V_out)·D/(L·f_sw); ΔV_cap = ΔiL/(8·C·f_sw); ΔV_ESR = ΔiL·ESR; ΔV_out = ΔV_cap + ΔV_ESR (worst-case linear sum per Erickson §2.4). CCM validity: iL_min = I_load − ΔiL/2 > 0 flagged; small-ripple approximation warning when ΔiL/(2·I_load) > 30%; ESR-dominance flag when ESR > 1/(4π·C·f_sw). `electronics_compute_buck_ripple` LLM tool registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_electronics/__init__.py`. 24 tests green. HONEST: CCM only — DCM (iL_min < 0) NOT modelled; small-ripple approximation (Erickson §2.1) breaks above 30% load variation; D = V_out/V_in is ideal (no deadtime, body-diode drop, or min-on-pulse); ESR assumed resistive/frequency-flat (use datasheet ESR at f_sw); ΔV_out is pessimistic linear sum (RSS is ~3–15% less pessimistic) — `packages/kerf-electronics/src/kerf_electronics/dc_dc_ripple.py`. Refs: Erickson "Fundamentals of Power Electronics" 3e §2.1, §2.4 Eq 2.34+2.36; Sandler "Power Electronics" §3; TI SLVA477.

**MOLD-RUNNER-DIAMETER-OPTIMIZE** ✅ — Optimal cold-runner diameter recommendation using the Beaumont (2007) §6.5 empirical formula D=(W^0.25×√L)/3.7, balancing fill pressure against cold-runner waste. `optimize_runner_diameter(RunnerOptimizeSpec) -> RunnerOptimizeReport` in `kerf_mold.runner_diameter_optimize`. Dataclasses: `RunnerOptimizeSpec` (part_weight_g, runner_length_mm, polymer_grade, gate_count=1); `RunnerOptimizeReport` (recommended_diameter_mm, beaumont_diameter_mm, cold_runner_waste_g, fill_pressure_estimate_MPa, polymer_specific_adjustment, honest_caveat). Algorithm: D_base=(W_eff^0.25×√L)/3.7 where W_eff=W/gate_count; material-viscosity adjustment: ABS+10%, PC+15% (highly viscous), PP-5% (low viscosity), PA66±0%; D clamped to [1.5, 16.0] mm. Cold-runner waste = π·(D/2)²·L × ρ_polymer/1000 [g]; polymer densities: ABS 1.05, PC 1.20, PP 0.91, PA66 1.14 g/cm³ (Menges 2001 Table 2.1). Fill-pressure proxy: P≈K_mat·L/D^4 (Hagen-Poiseuille analogy, order-of-magnitude only). `mold_optimize_runner_diameter` LLM tool registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_mold/__init__.py`. 28 tests green. HONEST: empirical formula only — NOT a full Hele-Shaw or Cross-WLF rheological simulation; optimises a SINGLE runner segment for one gate — does NOT optimise filling balance in multi-cavity molds (use mold_check_runner_balance + mold_generate_runner_layout for multi-cavity networks); fill-pressure estimate is order-of-magnitude proxy only; cold-runner waste assumes cylindrical cross-section (trapezoidal/half-round runners have different volumes); confirm with Moldflow/Moldex3D/SigmaSoft fill simulation and mold trial — `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/runner_diameter_optimize.py`. Refs: Beaumont 2007 §6.5 (Optimal runner diameter); Menges 2001 §6.5.

**MOLD-WARPAGE-INDEX** ✅ — Heuristic warpage-risk index (0–100) for injection-moulded parts. `compute_warpage_index(WarpageSpec) -> WarpageIndexReport` in `kerf_mold.warpage_index`. Dataclasses: `WarpageSpec` (wall_thickness_uniformity_pct: 0–100, gate_location: "centered"|"edge"|"corner"|"unbalanced", polymer_grade, post_eject_cooling_time_s, mold_temp_C); `WarpageIndexReport` (warpage_index: float, risk_level: "low"|"medium"|"high"|"severe", primary_warp_driver, mitigation_suggestions: list[str], honest_caveat, sub_scores: dict). Scoring (Beaumont 2007 §10 + Menges 2001 §8): wall-uniformity penalty (0–30 pts; piecewise linear: 100%→0 pts, 80%→6 pts, 0%→30 pts); gate-location penalty (0–25 pts: centered=3, edge=14, corner=22, unbalanced=25); polymer grade (0–20 pts: PC=5 low, ABS=7, PP=14 semi-cryst., POM=15, GF-PA66=20 max — Menges 2001 Table 8.2 shrinkage anisotropy); post-eject cooling time (0–15 pts; exponential decay score=15·exp(−t/40), characteristic time 40 s per Menges 2001 §8.5 HDT stabilisation); mold temperature deviation from recommended range (0–10 pts). Risk thresholds: 0–24 low, 25–49 medium, 50–74 high, 75–100 severe. Prioritised mitigation suggestions generated per dominant factor. `mold_compute_warpage_index` LLM tool registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_mold/__init__.py`. 39 tests green. HONEST: heuristic screening tool ONLY (±15 pts uncertainty typical) — real warpage prediction requires full filling + packing + cooling FEM simulation (Moldflow, Moldex3D, SigmaSoft 3D Warp); orientation-dependent shrinkage tensors, part geometry, packing pressure, injection speed, hold time, runner imbalance, sequential valve gating, and residual-stress relaxation are NOT modelled — `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/warpage_index.py`. Refs: Beaumont 2007 §10 (Warpage Analysis); Menges 2001 §8 (Post-mold shrinkage).

**MOLD-COOLING-PRESSURE-DROP** ✅ — Total pressure-drop across multi-segment mold cooling-channel networks (Darcy-Weisbach + minor-loss K-factors) + chiller pump head verification. `compute_cooling_pressure_drop(segments, coolant) -> CoolingPressureDropReport` in `kerf_mold.cooling_pressure_drop`. Dataclasses: `CoolingChannelSegment` (length_mm, diameter_mm, segment_type: "straight"|"elbow_90"|"elbow_45"|"tee_thru"|"tee_branch"); `CoolantSpec` (flow_rate_L_per_min, density_kg_m3=1000, viscosity_cP=1.0); `CoolingPressureDropReport` (total_pressure_drop_bar, reynolds_number, friction_factor, segment_breakdown, chiller_head_required_bar, recommended_pump_head_bar, honest_caveat). Algorithm: Re=ρ·v·D/μ; ΔP_major=f·(L/D)·(ρv²/2); ΔP_minor=K·(ρv²/2). Smooth-pipe friction: f=64/Re (laminar Re<2300); Blasius f=0.316/Re^0.25 (turbulent Re>4000); linear blend in transition. K-factors: elbow_90=0.9, elbow_45=0.4, tee_thru=0.6, tee_branch=1.8. Recommended pump head=total_ΔP×1.25 (25% margin). `mold_compute_cooling_pressure_drop` LLM tool registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_mold/__init__.py`. 24 tests green. HONEST: single-phase incompressible fluid only (water/water-glycol) — no two-phase/boiling flow; no heat-transfer coupling (viscosity spatially uniform); smooth-pipe Blasius only (no Colebrook-White roughness correction); series network assumed (parallel branches need per-branch analysis) — `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/cooling_pressure_drop.py`. Refs: Beaumont 2007 §11.2 Table 11.1; White "Fluid Mechanics" 8th ed. §6.7, §6.9.

**ELEC-EMI-FILTER-CUTOFF** ✅ — Passive LC/RC power-line EMI filter design per Ott "EMC Engineering" §15.3 + CISPR 22/EN 55022. `design_emi_filter(EmiFilterSpec) -> EmiFilterReport` in `kerf_electronics.emi_filter_design`. Dataclasses: `EmiFilterSpec` (dc_voltage_V, dc_current_A, target_attenuation_dB, target_freq_kHz, filter_topology, load_resistance_ohm=None); `EmiFilterReport` (cutoff_freq_Hz, L_uH, C_uF, R_ohm, attenuation_at_target_dB, recommended_caps_X2_uF, honest_caveat). Three topologies: LC_low_pass (2nd-order −40 dB/dec: f_c = f_t / 10^(A/40), C = 1/((2π·f_c)²·L) for L=100 µH); PI_LC_L (3rd-order π-section −60 dB/dec: f_c = f_t / 10^(A/60), each shunt cap = C/2); RC_low_pass (1st-order −20 dB/dec: f_c = f_t / 10^(A/20), C = 1/(2π·f_c·R)). X2 capacitor selection from IEC 60384-14 E12 series (275 VAC, 0.01–4.7 µF). `electronics_design_emi_filter` LLM tool registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_electronics/__init__.py`. 27 tests green. HONEST: ideal passive components only — no ESR, no winding stray capacitance, no parasitic cap inductance; DM-only (add CM choke separately); source/load assumed ideal (0 Ω / ∞ Ω); CISPR 22 Class B conducted limits (66–56 dBµV 0.15–0.50 MHz, 56 dBµV 0.50–5 MHz) cited for context only — accredited EMC lab measurement required for compliance — `packages/kerf-electronics/src/kerf_electronics/emi_filter_design.py`. Refs: Ott §15.3; CISPR 22 / EN 55022 4th ed. 2003; Nave 1991.

**CAM-TURNING-DEPTH** ✅ — Optimal depth-of-cut (DOC) per pass + total roughing passes for a lathe turning operation. `compute_turning_depth(TurningSpec) -> TurningDepthReport` in `kerf_cam.turning_depth_calc`. Dataclasses: `TurningSpec` (stock_diameter_mm, final_diameter_mm, finish_pass_doc_mm=0.5, max_roughing_doc_mm=3.0, material, tool_nose_radius_mm, feed_mm_per_rev, spindle_rpm, workpiece_length_mm=100); `TurningDepthReport` (num_roughing_passes, num_finishing_passes, total_passes, roughing_doc_mm, total_machining_time_s, recommended_doc_for_material, honest_caveat). Algorithm: radial_stock = (D_stock−D_final)/2; stock_for_roughing = radial_stock − finish_pass_doc; max_doc clamped to Sandvik CoroPlus / MH 31e §1148 material max; num_roughing = ceil(stock_for_roughing / effective_max_doc); roughing_doc = stock_for_roughing / num_roughing (equal passes); time_per_pass = workpiece_length / (feed × rpm/60). Material DOC ranges: steel_1018 2–4 mm (rec 3.0), aluminum_6061 4–8 mm (rec 6.0), stainless_303 1.5–2.5 mm (rec 2.0). Nose-radius check: warn if finish_pass_doc < 0.5×r_ε (MH 31e §1148 rubbing risk). `cam_compute_turning_depth` LLM tool registered in plugin.py. 38 tests green. HONEST: straight (cylindrical) turning only — no profile turning, no taper, no threading, no facing; Constant Surface Speed (CSS/G96) NOT implemented; time estimate excludes rapids, tool changes, and acceleration ramps; DOC ranges are conservative averages for coated carbide inserts at moderate cutting speed — verify against CoroPlus ToolGuide for production — `packages/kerf-cam/src/kerf_cam/turning_depth_calc.py`. Refs: MH 31e §1148; Sandvik CoroPlus Turning Catalogue (2024).

**ARCH-WIND-COMPONENT-CLADDING** ✅ — Design wind pressure on building components and cladding (C&C) per ASCE 7-22 §30.3. `compute_wind_cc_pressure(WindSiteSpec, BuildingSpec, ComponentSpec) -> WindCCPressureReport` in `kerf_cad_core.arch.wind_component_cladding`. Dataclasses: `ComponentSpec` (area_ft2, zone, component_type "wall"|"roof"); `WindCCPressureReport` (qz_psf, GCp_positive, GCp_negative, p_design_positive_psf, p_design_negative_psf, ASD_or_LRFD, code_section, honest_caveat). Six pressure zones: Zone_1_interior_wall (+0.9/−1.1 @ 10 ft²), Zone_4_wall_edge (+1.0/−1.1), Zone_5_corner_wall (+1.0/−1.4), Zone_1_roof_interior (+0.3/−1.0 @ 10 ft²), Zone_2_roof_edge (+0.3/−1.8), Zone_3_roof_corner (+0.3/−2.8) per Fig 30.3-2A/C. Log-linear effective-area GCp reduction: wall [10→500 ft²]; roof [10→100 ft²]. GCpi = ±0.18 enclosed (Table 26.13-1): p_pos = qh·(GCp_pos+0.18); p_neg = qh·(GCp_neg−0.18). `arch_compute_wind_cc_pressure` LLM tool registered via gated import; re-exported from `kerf_cad_core.arch` as `CCComponentSpec`. 53 tests green. HONEST: h ≤ 60 ft (§30.3 Low-Rise) only — §30.4 All-Heights not implemented; enclosed buildings only — partially-enclosed GCpi=±0.55 (§26.13.2) NOT modelled; roof slopes >7° (Fig 30.3-2D) not implemented; parapets (§30.9) not implemented; minimum pressure ±16 psf (§30.2.2) not auto-enforced — `packages/kerf-cad-core/src/kerf_cad_core/arch/wind_component_cladding.py`. Refs: ASCE/SEI 7-22 §26.13.2, §30.1, §30.3 Eq 30.3-1, Fig 30.3-2A, Fig 30.3-2C.

**ARCH-WIND-LOAD-ASCE7** ✅ — Design wind pressure on building walls per ASCE 7-22 §26–27 Directional Procedure (MWFRS). `compute_wind_load(WindSiteSpec, BuildingSpec) -> WindPressureReport` in `kerf_cad_core.arch.wind_load_asce7`. Dataclasses: `WindSiteSpec` (V_basic_mph, exposure_category "B"/"C"/"D", K_zt, risk_category); `BuildingSpec` (mean_height_h_ft, length_ft, width_ft, enclosure); `WindPressureReport` (qz_psf, Kz, Cp_windward, Cp_leeward, p_windward_psf, p_leeward_psf, total_drag_psf, L_over_B, code_section, honest_caveat). Exposure constants: B α=7.0/zg=1200 ft, C α=9.5/zg=900 ft, D α=11.5/zg=700 ft (Table 26.10-1). Velocity pressure qz = 0.00256·Kz·Kzt·Kd·V² (Kd=0.85 buildings). Kz = 2.01·(z/zg)^(2/α), floored at z=15 ft. Windward Cp=+0.8; leeward Cp: −0.5 (L/B≤1), −0.3 (L/B=2), −0.2 (L/B≥4), linearly interpolated. Gust factor G=0.85 (rigid). `arch_compute_wind_load` LLM tool registered via gated import; re-exported from `kerf_cad_core.arch`. 24 tests green. HONEST: Directional Procedure (§27) only — Envelope Procedure (§28) not implemented; tornado loads (§32) not implemented; internal pressure coefficient GCpi (§26.13) excluded (add separately for component design); parapet loads (§27.7) and roof pressures excluded; flexible-building dynamic G (§26.11.2) not supported; V_basic_mph must match the correct risk-category map (Fig 26.5-1 RC II; 26.5-2A/B/C others) — `packages/kerf-cad-core/src/kerf_cad_core/arch/wind_load_asce7.py`. Refs: ASCE/SEI 7-22 §26.6, §26.10 Eq 26.10-1, §26.11, §27.3, §27.4 Eq 27.4-1, Fig 27.4-1.

**GDT-FEATURE-OF-SIZE-DOF (ASME Y14.5-2018 §4.7 + §7.3)** ✅ — `compute_fos_dof(FOSSpec) -> FOSDoFReport` enumerates the Degrees of Freedom constrained vs released by a Feature of Size + geometric tolerance combination — critical for inspection planning. Dataclasses: `FOSSpec` (feature_type: "cylinder"|"hole"|"slot"|"sphere"|"planar_pair"|"width", tolerance_symbol: "position"|"perpendicularity"|"parallelism"|"angularity"|"runout"|"total_runout"); `FOSDoFReport` (dof_constrained, dof_released, total_constrained, datum_required_count, code_section, honest_caveat). DOF rules per §4.7 + §7.3: cylinder/hole + position → TX, TY (axis radial location); cylinder/hole + orientation → RX, RY (axis tilt); cylinder/hole + runout/total_runout → TX, TY, RX, RY (§7.3.4/§7.3.5 coupling); slot/width/planar_pair + position → TX (centre-plane location); slot + orientation → RX, RY; sphere + position → TX, TY, TZ (point location); sphere + orientation → nothing (rotationally symmetric). `gdt_compute_fos_dof` LLM tool registered via gated import pattern; registered in plugin.py `_TOOL_MODULES`; re-exported from `kerf_cad_core.gdt`. 35 tests green. HONEST FLAG: feature-class lookup table only — pattern-of-features compositions (§11.3) where DOFs compound across multiple instances are not modelled; PLTZF/FRTZF interactions (§10.5) not resolved; coordinate-frame orientation is a modelling assumption (cylinder axis assumed along Z) — caller must orient TX/TY/TZ/RX/RY/RZ to the actual drawing DRF — `packages/kerf-cad-core/src/kerf_cad_core/gdt/feature_of_size_dof.py`.

**GDT-DATUM-SHIFT-CHECK (ASME Y14.5-2018 §4.5 + §7.3.5)** ✅ — `compute_datum_shift(DatumFeatureSpec, base_position_tolerance_mm) -> DatumShiftReport` computes per-datum bonus tolerance (datum shift) when a datum feature of size is referenced with an MMC or LMC modifier in the feature control frame. Dataclasses: `DatumFeatureSpec` (datum_letter, mmc_size_mm, lmc_size_mm, measured_size_mm, material_condition_modifier); `DatumShiftReport` (datum_letter, base_tolerance_zone_mm, bonus_shift_mm, total_available_tolerance_mm, shift_allowed, code_section, honest_caveat). Computation per §4.5 + §7.3.5: MMC modifier → shift = |measured − MMC|; LMC modifier → shift = |measured − LMC|; RFS → shift = 0. Total available tolerance = base + bonus_shift. `gdt_compute_datum_shift` LLM tool registered via gated import pattern; re-exported from `kerf_cad_core.gdt`. 30 tests green. HONEST FLAG: per-datum shift computed independently — multi-datum DRF secondary/tertiary cascade constraint propagation (§4.11.4) is datum-by-datum; composite frame validation (PLTZF/FRTZF §10.5.2) is separate in `composite_tolerance_check` — `packages/kerf-cad-core/src/kerf_cad_core/gdt/datum_shift_check.py`.

**GDT-COMPOSITE-TOLERANCE (ASME Y14.5-2018 §10.5.2 + §11.6)** ✅ — `validate_composite_frame(CompositeFrameSpec) -> CompositeFrameValidationReport` validates stacked PLTZF/FRTZF composite feature control frames in `kerf_cad_core.gdt.composite_tolerance_check`. Dataclasses: `CompositeTolSegment` (symbol, tol_value_mm, datum_refs, material_condition); `CompositeFrameSpec` (feature_id, segments list); `CompositeFrameValidationReport` (valid, violations, standard_section, honest_caveat). Three rules enforced: R1 — all segments share the same geometric symbol (§10.5.2(a)); R2 — each lower segment tolerance ≤ segment above it (FRTZF tol ≤ PLTZF tol, §10.5.1 Note 2); R3 — lower segment datum_refs must be a subset of the segment above (§10.5.1(b)) — new datums below the PLTZF would imply location constraint, reserved for the PLTZF; FRTZF may only refine orientation. Multi-tier (3+ segment) composite frames supported. `gdt_validate_composite_frame` LLM tool registered via gated import pattern; re-exported from `kerf_cad_core.gdt`. HONEST FLAG: validates frame structure only — does not verify inspection measurement data against tolerance zones, does not parse drawing text, and does not check geometric compatibility with the part model. 44 tests green — `packages/kerf-cad-core/src/kerf_cad_core/gdt/composite_tolerance_check.py`.

**SUBD-LIMIT-NORMAL-FIT** ✅ — sample the Catmull-Clark limit-surface normal n̂(u,v) at a uniform (u,v) grid across all cage faces using Stam (1998) exact eigenstructure tangent vectors; `sample_subd_limit_normals(cage_mesh, samples_per_face=9, normalize=True)` returns `LimitNormalFitResult(sampled_normals, max_normal_residual_deg, mean_normal_residual_deg, num_irregular_samples, honest_caveat)`; per-face n×n grid (n = round(sqrt(samples_per_face))); normal via N = ∂S/∂u × ∂S/∂v from Stam tangents (C¹-continuous at extraordinary vertices, exact bi-cubic B-spline for valence-4 regular faces); residuals computed against bilinear interpolation of four face-corner Stam normals — quantifies accuracy gain of a proper normal field vs the simple shader approximation; irregular-vertex flag per sample (valence ≠ 4 faces); LLM tool `subd_sample_limit_normals` registered in plugin via gated import; re-exported from `kerf_cad_core.subd`; 17 oracle-asserted tests (flat plane nz > 0.9999, unit-length all faces, nx/ny ≈ 0, dot > 0.9999, normalize=True/False, result structure, total sample count, honest_caveat non-empty, irregular cube valence-3 > 0, flat plane residual < 0.5°, max residual ≤ 90°, cylinder normals perpendicular to Y, cube 24-sample count + unit-length, empty cage no exception). HONEST: "fit" = residual analysis vs bilinear, NOT a closed-form NURBS surface (would require overdetermined least-squares + knot/CP storage) — `kerf-cad-core/src/kerf_cad_core/subd/limit_normal_fit.py`. Refs: Stam (1998) §3.2; Halstead-Kass-DeRose (1993); Piegl-Tiller §9.

**ARCH-BASE-PLATE-AISC (AISC DG-1 §3.1 + AISC 360-22 §J8)** ✅ — `design_base_plate(ColumnSpec, ConcreteSpec, Fy=345.0) -> BasePlateReport` implements steel column base plate design for concentric axial compressive loads. Concrete bearing strength: Pp = 0.85·f'c·A1·√(A2/A1) with A2/A1 ≤ 4 (AISC 360-22 §J8 Eq J8-2); φ_c = 0.65; required A1 = P_u/(φ_c·0.85·f'c·√(A2/A1)). Plate dimensions rounded up to nearest 5 mm; must cover column footprint (0.95·d × 0.80·bf per DG-1 §3.1.1). Cantilever arms: m=(N−0.95·d)/2 (Eq 3.1-1); n=(B−0.80·bf)/2 (Eq 3.1-2); n'=√(d·bf)/4; X=[4·d·bf/(d+bf)²]·[P_u/(φ_c·Pp)] (Eq 3.1-8); λ=min(1, 2·√X/(1+√(1−X))); l=max(m,n,λ·n'). Plate thickness via Murray-Stockwell (DG-1 Eq 3.1-5): t=l·√(2·P_u/(0.9·Fy·B·N)), rounded up to 1 mm. Oracle: W14x90, P=1000 kN, f'c=30 MPa, ped 600×600 mm → A1_req≈30166 mm²; plate 295×340 mm (column footprint governs, N_min=338 mm, B_min=295 mm); t=15 mm; DCR=0.318 (adequate). `arch_design_base_plate` LLM tool registered in plugin (gated import). Re-exported from arch/__init__.py. 24 hermetic oracle tests pass — `packages/kerf-cad-core/src/kerf_cad_core/arch/base_plate_aisc.py`. *SCOPE: concentric axial compressive load ONLY (DG-1 §3.1). NOT covered: moment transfer (DG-1 §3.2), anchor rod design (DG-1 §3.3–3.4), shear lug (DG-1 §3.5), biaxial bending, tensile uplift. A2 taken as pedestal plan area; irregular pedestals must supply equivalent rectangular A2. Grout strength ≥ f'c assumed.*

**ARCH-BEAM-DEFLECTION (Roark 9e §8 + AISC Manual Table 3-23)** ✅ — `compute_beam_deflection(BeamSpec) -> BeamDeflectionReport` implements five closed-form Euler-Bernoulli beam cases: (1) simply_supported + point_center: δ=PL³/(48EI), M=PL/4 [Roark Table 8.1 case 7; AISC 3-23 diag 1]; (2) simply_supported + udl: δ=5wL⁴/(384EI), M=wL²/8 [case 2; diag 2]; (3) cantilever + point_center (tip load): δ=PL³/(3EI), M=PL [case 1; diag 6]; (4) cantilever + udl: δ=wL⁴/(8EI), M=wL²/2 [case 3; diag 7]; (5) fixed_fixed + udl: δ=wL⁴/(384EI), M=wL²/12 [case 15; diag 9]. `BeamDeflectionReport` returns δ_max_mm, M_max_Nmm, V_max_N, deflection_location_mm, honest_caveat. `arch_compute_beam_deflection` LLM tool registered in plugin; gated import (registry unavailable → module still importable). 39 hermetic oracle tests pass (formula verification ≤0.1%; W14x90 L=6 m P=100 kN δ≈5.41 mm hand-verified; zero-load→zero; fixed_fixed+point_center → ValueError; invalid inputs → ValueError; re-export from arch/__init__.py) — `packages/kerf-cad-core/src/kerf_cad_core/arch/beam_deflection.py`. *Scope: linear-elastic, small-deflection Euler-Bernoulli only. No shear deformation (Timoshenko), no lateral-torsional buckling, no yield check, no partial-span loads.*

**ARCH-COLUMN-LOAD-CHECK (AISC 360-22 §E3 + ACI 318-19 §22.4)** ✅ — `check_steel_column(SteelColumnSpec, P_kN) -> ColumnLoadReport` implements AISC 360-22 §E3 LRFD: Fe = π²E/(KL/r)², inelastic Fcr = 0.658^(Fy/Fe)·Fy (E3-2) for KL/r ≤ 4.71√(E/Fy), elastic Fcr = 0.877·Fe (E3-3) otherwise, φ_c = 0.90, slender-column flag at KL/r > 200. `check_concrete_column(ConcreteColumnSpec, P_kN) -> ColumnLoadReport` implements ACI 318-19 §22.4.2.2: φ·Pn = φ·0.80·[0.85·f'c·(Ag−Ast) + fy·Ast], φ = 0.65 tied (0.75 spiral), ρg bounds check per §10.6.1.1. Both return `ColumnLoadReport` with φPn, DCR, governing mode, PASS/FAIL, and honest caveat. `arch_check_column_load` LLM tool registered in plugin. 27 hermetic oracle tests pass (W14x90 at KL=4 000 mm formula-verified; ACI concrete 400×400 formula-verified; DCR > 1.0 FAIL; KL/r > 200 warning; ValueError on bad inputs; tool ok/err payloads) — `packages/kerf-cad-core/src/kerf_cad_core/arch/column_load_check.py`. *Disclaimer: local buckling, torsional buckling, combined loading, and slenderness amplification (ACI §6.6.4) not included.*

**ARCH-FOOTING-BEARING-CAPACITY (Meyerhof 1963 / Bowles 5e §4 / Das 8e §3)** ✅ — `compute_bearing_capacity(FootingSpec, SoilProperties, FS=3.0) -> BearingCapacityReport` implements the Meyerhof (1963) general bearing capacity equation q_ult = c·N_c·s_c·d_c + γ·Df·N_q·s_q·d_q + 0.5·γ·B·N_γ·s_γ·d_γ for shallow footings on cohesive/cohesionless soil. N-factors: N_q = e^(π·tanφ)·tan²(45+φ/2); N_c = (N_q−1)·cotφ (φ=0: N_c=5.14 Prandtl limit); N_γ = (N_q−1)·tan(1.4φ). Shape factors s_c, s_q, s_γ per Bowles Table 4-4 for strip/square/circular/rectangular. Depth factors d_c, d_q, d_γ per Bowles Table 4-4. q_allow = q_ult / FS (default 3.0). `BearingCapacityReport` returns q_ult_kPa, q_allow_kPa, FS, N_c/N_q/N_γ, s_c, d_c, honest_caveat. `arch_compute_bearing_capacity` LLM tool registered in plugin; gated import pattern. 25 hermetic oracle tests pass (φ=30°: N_c=30.14, N_q=18.40, N_γ=15.67 within 1%; φ=0 clay 50 kPa square 2×2m Df=1m formula verified q_ult=357.24 kPa; strip s=1; square s>1; depth factors increase with Df/B; custom FS; rectangular interpolation; ValueError on bad inputs; re-export from arch/__init__.py) — `packages/kerf-cad-core/src/kerf_cad_core/arch/footing_bearing.py`. *Scope: Meyerhof (1963) shape+depth factors only. No Brinch Hansen rigidity index (I_r) correction, no inclined/eccentric loads, no seismic, no liquefaction, no layered-soil punching-shear.*

**ARCH-SLAB-DEFLECTION (Timoshenko §44 Tables 41–42 + Roark 9e Table 11.4)** ✅ — `compute_slab_deflection(SlabSpec, LoadSpec) -> SlabDeflectionReport` implements closed-form center-point deflection for two-way rectangular slabs under uniform load via Kirchhoff thin-plate theory: δ_max = α·q·a⁴/D; D = E·h³/(12·(1−ν²)). Boundary conditions: (1) all-edges-simply-supported (AESS) — α from Timoshenko Table 41, linearly interpolated at any a/b ≥ 1; key values: a/b=1.0 α=0.00406, a/b=1.5 α=0.00772, a/b=2.0 α=0.01013, a/b→∞ α=0.01302 (one-way strip limit); (2) all-edges-fixed (AEFC) — α from Timoshenko Table 42: a/b=1.0 α=0.00126 (exact); other ratios scaled-interpolation approximation. Moment outputs: M_xx = β_x·q·a², M_yy = β_y·q·a² (Timoshenko Table 41 β coefficients). `SlabDeflectionReport` returns delta_max_mm, M_max_xx_Nmm_per_mm, M_max_yy_Nmm_per_mm, plate_stiffness_D, honest_caveat. `arch_compute_slab_deflection` LLM tool registered in plugin; gated import pattern (registry unavailable → still importable). 21 hermetic oracle tests pass (α=0.00406 within 1%; a/b=2 α=0.01013; a/b=1.5 α=0.00772; h³ stiffness scaling; load linearity; FF < SS δ; FF α=0.00126; zero load → zero; D exact; one-way limit; M≥0; all 6 validation error paths; re-export; dimension-order symmetry) — `packages/kerf-cad-core/src/kerf_cad_core/arch/slab_deflection.py`. *Scope: linear-elastic Kirchhoff thin plate only. NOT included: shear deformation (Mindlin — significant for h/a > ~0.1); plastic hinge redistribution; concrete cracking / tension stiffening; creep / shrinkage; orthotropic / ribbed slabs; punching shear; exact Timoshenko double-series for intermediate fixed-fixed a/b ratios.*

**ARCH-DIAPHRAGM-SHEAR (AWC SDPWS-2021 §4.2 + SDI DDM04 + IBC §2305.2)** ✅ — `check_diaphragm_shear(DiaphragmSpec, V_lateral_lbs, phi=0.65) -> DiaphragmShearReport` implements in-plane shear capacity check for horizontal wood structural panel and cold-formed steel (metal deck) diaphragms (floor or roof). Wood (plywood / OSB): v = V/L (plf); v_allow from SDPWS-2021 Table 4.2A (8d common nails, DF_L reference), linearly interpolated for intermediate nail spacings; species factor C_s (DF_L/SP=1.00, HF=0.90, SPF=0.80); unblocked reduction 0.50× (§4.2.7 Case 1). **ARCH-BEARING-WALL-AXIAL (ACI 318-19 §11.5.3.1 + TMS 402-22 §8.3 + Wight §13.13)** ✅ — `check_bearing_wall(BearingWallSpec, P_factored_kN_per_m, phi=0.65) -> BearingWallReport` implements axial-load capacity of plain concrete, reinforced concrete, and masonry bearing walls (unit-strip per metre width). ACI 318-19 §11.5.3.1 (concrete/reinforced_concrete): φ·Pn = 0.55·φ·f'c·Ag·[1−(k·lc/(32·t))²]; k from end_conditions: fixed_fixed=0.8, pin_pin=1.0, cantilever=2.0 (ACI Commentary R11.5.3.1). **ARCH-PIER-AXIAL (TMS 402-22 §8.3 + ACI 318-19 §22.4.2.2 + Drysdale-Hamid §10)** ✅ — `check_pier_axial(PierSpec, P_factored_kN, phi=0.65) -> PierAxialReport` implements axial-load capacity of slender masonry and reinforced concrete piers with TMS Eq 8-22 h/r slenderness reduction. Materials: clay_masonry + concrete_masonry (TMS §8.3): φ·Pn = φ·0.80·f'm·Ag·C_s; reinforced_concrete (ACI §22.4.2.2): φ·Pn = φ·0.80·[0.85·f'c·(Ag−As)+fy·As]·C_s. Radius of gyration: r = min(pier_width, pier_thickness) / √12 (governing weak-axis r for rectangular section). Effective height: h_eff = k·h per end_conditions — fixed_fixed k=0.5, pin_pin k=1.0, fixed_pin k=0.7, cantilever k=2.0 (Drysdale-Hamid §10). `PierAxialReport` returns phi_Pn_kN, slenderness_factor, h_over_r, governing_failure_mode (yielding|slender_buckling|slenderness_limit_exceeded), honest_caveat. Oracle (200×200mm pin-pin h=3000mm clay_masonry f'm=10MPa): r=57.7mm, h/r=52.0, C_s=1−(3000/(140×57.7))²≈0.862, φ·Pn≈179.5 kN; h/r>99 (e.g. h=6000mm pin-pin) → slenderness_limit_exceeded; fixed_fixed → smaller h_eff → larger C_s; RC path verifies ACI §22.4.2.2 contribution. `arch_check_pier_axial` LLM tool registered in plugin (gated import); re-exported from arch/__init__.py. 49 hermetic oracle tests pass — `packages/kerf-cad-core/src/kerf_cad_core/arch/pier_axial_capacity.py`. *SCOPE: Concentric axial load ONLY — eccentricity, moment interaction (PM curve), and combined axial+bending NOT modelled. **ARCH-RETAINING-WALL-STABILITY (Bowles 5e §12.3 + Das §13 — Rankine active)** ✅ — `check_retaining_wall(RetainingWallSpec, SoilSpec) -> RetainingWallReport` implements overturning, sliding, and bearing stability checks for cantilevered concrete retaining walls under Rankine active earth pressure. Ka = tan²(45−φ/2); Pa = 0.5·γ_s·H²·Ka (horizontal resultant, at H/3). Weight components per metre: W_stem = γ_c·t·(H−h); W_base = γ_c·B·h; W_soil = γ_s·l_heel·(H−h). Moments about toe: M_resist = W_stem·(l_toe+t/2) + W_base·(B/2) + W_soil·(B−l_heel/2); M_overt = Pa·(H/3). FoS_overturning = M_resist/M_overt (min 2.0). FoS_sliding = ΣW·tan(δ)/Pa (min 1.5). Bearing: e = B/2 − (M_resist−M_overt)/ΣW; q_max = (ΣW/B)·(1+6e/B) (trapezoidal; triangular when e>B/6); FoS_bearing = q_a/q_max (min 3.0). `RetainingWallReport` returns Ka, Pa_kN_per_m, FoS_overturning, FoS_sliding, q_max_kPa, FoS_bearing, all_adequate, governing_failure_mode, honest_caveat. Oracle (H=3m, B=2m, t=0.3m, h=0.3m, l_heel=1.5m, l_toe=0.2m, γ_c=24, γ_s=18, φ=30°): Ka=1/3, Pa=27.0 kN/m, FoS_overt=4.16 (adequate), FoS_sliding=1.44 (inadequate at δ=20°; adequate at δ=25°). `arch_check_retaining_wall_stability` LLM tool registered in plugin (gated import); re-exported from arch/__init__.py. 27 hermetic oracle tests pass — `packages/kerf-cad-core/src/kerf_cad_core/arch/retaining_wall_stability.py`. *SCOPE: Rankine ACTIVE pressure only — level backfill, cohesionless (c=0). NO surcharge load. NO seismic (Mononobe-Okabe, AASHTO LRFD §11.6.5 / Das §13.12). NO passive resistance from toe soil (conservative). NO hydrostatic pressure (free-draining assumed). Bearing: trapezoidal pressure distribution; triangular applied automatically for e>B/6. Always verify with a licensed geotechnical/structural engineer.*

**ARCH-SHEAR-WALL-OOP (ACI 318-19 §11.7 + §22.3 + Wight §13.13)** ✅ — `check_shear_wall_oop(ShearWallSpec, phi=0.65) -> ShearWallOOPReport` implements out-of-plane (OOP) flexural capacity check for RC shear walls under combined axial + lateral (wind/seismic) loads. **ARCH-PUNCHING-SHEAR (ACI 318-19 §22.6 + Wight §13.10)** ✅ — `check_punching_shear(ColumnSlabSpec, V_applied_kN, phi=0.75) -> PunchingShearReport` implements two-way (punching) shear capacity check for flat concrete slabs around columns per ACI 318-19 §22.6. Governing vc = min of ACI §22.6.5.2 three equations: (a) vc = 0.33·λ·√f'c [basic]; (b) vc = 0.17·(1+2/β_c)·λ·√f'c [aspect-ratio, governs when β_c > 2]; (c) vc = 0.083·(α_s·d/b_0+2)·λ·√f'c [perimeter, governs at corner with large column or high α_s·d/b_0 ratio]. Design strength: φ·Vn = φ·vc·b_0·d (φ=0.75 default, Table 21.2.1). `PunchingShearReport` returns b_0_mm, vc_basic/aspect/perimeter/governing_MPa, phi_vc_kN, demand_capacity_ratio, adequate, governing_eqn, honest_caveat. **ARCH-LATERAL-BRACING (AISC 360-22 §F2 + AISC Manual Table 3-2)** ✅ — `check_lateral_bracing(WSectionSpec, L_b_mm, Cb=1.0) -> LateralBracingReport` implements AISC 360-22 §F2 LRFD for compact doubly symmetric I-shaped members bent about the major axis. Equations: Lp = 1.76·ry·√(E/Fy) (F2-5); Lr = 1.95·rts·(E/0.7Fy)·√(Jc/Sxho + √((Jc/Sxho)²+6.76·(0.7Fy/E)²)) (F2-6); Zone 1 Lb≤Lp → Mn = Mp = Fy·Zx (F2-1, yielding); Zone 2 Lp<Lb≤Lr → Mn = Cb·[Mp−(Mp−0.7·Fy·Sx)·(Lb−Lp)/(Lr−Lp)]≤Mp (F2-2, inelastic_LTB); Zone 3 Lb>Lr → Mn = Fcr·Sx≤Mp, Fcr = Cb·π²E/(Lb/rts)²·√(1+0.078·Jc/(Sx·ho)·(Lb/rts)²) (F2-3/4, elastic_LTB). φ_b = 0.90; c=1.0 (F2-8a). `LateralBracingReport` returns Lp, Lr, Mp, Mr, Mn, phi_Mn, governing_mode ("yielding"|"inelastic_LTB"|"elastic_LTB"), Lb_to_Lp_ratio, honest_caveat. W14x90 oracle (Fy=345 MPa): Lp=3 983 mm (≈4.0 m), Lr=12 962 mm (≈13.0 m), Mp=887.6 kN·m, Mr=565.9 kN·m — consistent with AISC Manual Table 3-2. `arch_check_lateral_bracing` LLM tool registered in plugin (gated import). 27 hermetic tests pass — `packages/kerf-cad-core/src/kerf_cad_core/arch/lateral_bracing_check.py`. *SCOPE: doubly symmetric compact I-shaped members (W-shapes) ONLY. **BREP-SOLID-CONTAINS-POINT** ✅ — Ray-casting Jordan-curve inside/outside test for B-rep solids: `solid_contains_point(body, point, tolerance=1e-6) -> ContainmentResult` casts a generic-direction ray (1, 0.013, 0.029) from the query point and counts boundary crossings; odd = inside, even = outside. `ContainmentResult` dataclass: `inside` (bool|None), `on_boundary`, `ray_hits`, `degenerate_ray`. Planar faces use exact ray-polygon (loop vertices); analytic/NURBS faces use UV-grid triangulation (Möller-Trumbore per triangle, default 32×32 grid). Degenerate-ray honest flag: if primary direction is parallel to a face, fallback direction (0.017, 1, 0.011) is tried; if both disagree on parity, `degenerate_ray=True` and `inside=None`. ### Latest delta — 2026-05-31

**NURBS-CURVE-FRESNEL-PARAMETERIZE** ✅ — `fresnel_parameterize_curve(curve, num_samples=200, target_kappa_rate=1.0)` returns `FresnelParameterizationResult(curve_out, max_curvature_residual, fresnel_S, fresnel_C, honest_caveat)`; re-parameterizes a NurbsCurve so that curvature grows linearly with arc-length (κ(s) ≈ α·s — Euler spiral / clothoid / Cornu spiral law). Algorithm: (1) arc-length–uniform sampling via adaptive 5-pt Gauss-Legendre; (2) Fresnel integral evaluation C(σ), S(σ) with σ=s·√(α/π) (Abramowitz-Stegun §7.3); (3) monotone Fresnel-C parameter sequence drives NURBS re-interpolation (Piegl-Tiller §9.2); (4) monotone-blend fallback when spiral winds past first inflection. Degree-1 polyline caveat; zero-length degenerate guard; negative-alpha treated as positive. LLM tool `nurbs_fresnel_parameterize_curve` registered (gated import). Re-exported from `geom/__init__.py`. 25 hermetic tests. HONEST: sampling-based, not closed-form; Fresnel monotone blend active for long curves; curvature residual is approximate. Refs: Walton & Meek (2009) §§2–3; Bertolazzi & Frego (2015) §3 — `kerf-cad-core/geom/fresnel_parameterize.py`.

**NURBS-CURVE-INFLECTION** ✅ — `find_curve_inflections(curve_or_points, num_samples=200, threshold=1e-9)` returns `InflectionResult(inflection_t_params, num_inflections, signed_curvature_samples, honest_caveat)`; finds inflection points of a 2D NURBS curve where κ_signed(t) changes sign. Algorithm: sample κ_signed(t) = (x'y'' − y'x'')/|C'|³ at `num_samples` uniform t-values via NURBS analytical 1st/2nd derivatives (Piegl-Tiller §9.1/§9.2); detect adjacent-sample sign changes (threshold guards near-zero samples); refine each bracket with 5-iteration bisection. `signed_curvature_samples` returns full [(t, κ_signed)] profile. Also accepts raw `(t, κ)` sample sequences. Oracles: S-curve cubic → 1 inflection near t=0.5; two-arch sine → ≥2 inflections; circle → 0 inflections; straight line → 0 inflections + honest_caveat. LLM tool `nurbs_find_curve_inflections` registered (gated import). Re-exported from `geom/__init__.py`. 20 hermetic tests. HONEST: **2D only** — near-zero-curvature regions (|κ| < threshold) may produce false positives or suppress gentle crossings; straight line gives honest caveat about κ≡0. Applications: fairness analysis, sketch QC, toolpath transitions. Refs: do Carmo §1.5; Sapidis §3 — `kerf-cad-core/geom/curve_inflection.py`.

**NURBS-CURVE-EVOLUTE** ✅ — `compute_curve_evolute(curve, num_samples=200, min_curvature=1e-6)` returns `EvoluteResult(evolute_points, t_params, num_samples, num_cusps_detected, cusp_t_params, honest_caveat)`; computes the locus of centres of osculating circles E(t) = C(t) + n̂(t)/κ(t) where n̂ is the left-hand unit normal and κ is the signed curvature. Algorithm: sample t ∈ [t_min, t_max] at `num_samples` uniform points; evaluate κ(t) via standard plane-curve formula κ = (x'y'' − y'x'')/(x'²+y'²)^(3/2) using NURBS analytical derivatives; skip samples where |κ| < min_curvature (evolute diverges); detect cusps (vertices of C) as local extrema of |κ| via windowed comparison with amplitude guard (suppresses floating-point chatter on constant-κ curves). Circle oracle: all evolute points within 1.6e-15 of center. Parabola y=x²/2: apex evolute = (0,1) exactly. Ellipse a=2,b=1: 4 cusps (stretched-astroid evolute). Straight line: evolute empty. LLM tool `nurbs_compute_curve_evolute` registered (gated import). Re-exported from `geom/__init__.py`. 20 hermetic tests. HONEST: **2D curves only** — 3D Frenet-Serret evolutes (requiring torsion) are not yet supported; cusp detection is windowed/amplitude-gated and depends on sample density; may miss cusps for highly undersampled curves. Applications: cycloidal-gear design, cam-profile cusp analysis, CNC offset self-intersection prediction. Refs: do Carmo §1.6; Mortenson §4.2 — `kerf-cad-core/geom/curve_evolute.py`.

**NURBS-SURFACE-CROSS-SECTION** ✅ — `compute_surface_cross_section(surface, plane_point, plane_normal, nu=50, nv=50)` returns `SurfaceCrossSectionResult(intersection_points_3d, num_intersections, num_components, is_closed_loop, honest_caveat)`; computes the planar cross-section curve C(t) of a NurbsSurface S(u,v) intersected with a plane P (point + normal). Algorithm (Sederberg CAGD §7.3; Patrikalakis-Maekawa §5): (1) sample S(u,v) on a (nu × nv) uniform grid over the knot domain; (2) compute signed distance d(u,v) = (S − P) · n̂ for each sample; (3) walk all u-direction and v-direction grid edges, detect sign changes (d_A * d_B < 0); (4) refine each crossing via 5 bisection iterations in (u,v) parameter space (positional error ≈ cell_size/32); (5) chain intersection points into polyline components via greedy nearest-neighbour walk; (6) detect closed loops (first ≈ last point within 3× mean spacing). Oracles: sphere R=2 ∩ XY plane (mean radius within 20%), cylinder ∩ XZ plane (2 components, y≈0), flat patch ∩ parallel plane (empty), torus ∩ z=0 (inner/outer rings), non-unit normal idempotent, zero normal safe. LLM tool `nurbs_compute_surface_cross_section` registered via gated import. Re-exported from `geom/__init__.py`. 22 hermetic tests green. HONEST: **sample-based** — sub-cell features (thin necks, tangential near-grazing crossings) may be missed at low nu/nv; 5-iteration bisection (not sub-pixel for coarse grids); component ordering greedy nearest-neighbour (may mis-order interleaved loops); closed-loop detection threshold-based. Refs: Sederberg CAGD §7.3; Patrikalakis-Maekawa §5 — `kerf-cad-core/geom/surface_cross_section.py`.

**NURBS uniform arc-length resample** ✅ — `resample_uniform_arc_length(curve, samples=100)` returns `ResampleResult(points, parameters, arc_lengths, total_length, fitted_curve, degenerate)`; arc-length inversion via bisection on adaptive 5-pt Gauss-Legendre integral (Piegl-Tiller §9.4 + Patrikalakis-Maekawa §3.5); `fit=True` returns interpolated NurbsCurve; degenerate flag for zero-length curves; LLM tool `nurbs_curve_resample_uniform`; 12 analytic-oracle tests (circle 2π/100 ± 0.001, parabola arc-uniform < param-uniform variance, line sqrt(2)/10 ± 1e-6, degenerate flag). Honest: GL quadrature ~1e-9 accurate; highly-oscillatory curves may need larger `max_depth`.
**Mold MFR injection-speed check** ✅ — `mold_check_melt_flow_ratio` LLM tool: given a polymer's Melt Flow Rate (ASTM D1238 g/10 min), wall thickness, and gate type, returns the recommended injection-speed envelope to avoid jetting, sink marks, and gate freeze-off. Four MFR bands (low < 5, medium 5–25, high 25–100, super-high > 100 g/10 min); wall-thickness and gate-type correction factors applied; qualitative risk flags for gate freeze, jetting, and sink marks. References: Beaumont 2007 §4 + Menges 2001 §6.2 + ASTM D1238. **Honest caveat**: heuristic only — MFR is a single-point viscosity proxy; real injection-speed tuning requires full shear-thinning viscosity curve and on-tool DOE with cavity-pressure measurement — `kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/melt_flow_ratio_check.py`.

**MOLD-SPRUE-BUSHING-MATCH** ✅ — `check_sprue_bushing_match(SprueBushingSpec, MachineNozzleSpec) -> SprueMatchReport` in `kerf_mold.sprue_bushing_match`. Verifies that the cold-runner sprue bushing nozzle-seat radius (R) and orifice diameter (O) match the injection-moulding machine nozzle tip geometry per Beaumont 2007 §6.4 + DME standard sprue bushing catalogue §3.2. Compliance rules: sprue_R = nozzle_r + 0.5–1.0 mm; sprue_O = nozzle_O + 0.5–1.0 mm; taper 1.5–3.0°/side. Dataclasses: `SprueBushingSpec` (nozzle_radius_R_mm, sprue_orifice_diameter_O_mm, total_length_mm, taper_per_side_deg); `MachineNozzleSpec` (nozzle_tip_radius_mm, nozzle_tip_orifice_diameter_mm); `SprueMatchReport` (R_mismatch_mm, R_compliant, O_mismatch_mm, O_compliant, taper_compliant, recommendation, honest_caveat). LLM tool `mold_check_sprue_bushing_match` registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_mold/__init__.py`. 35 oracle tests green. **HONEST SCOPE: standard cold-runner sprue bushings only** — hot-runner nozzle seats (DME hot-tip, valve-gate, edge-gate) follow different design rules (thermal expansion allowance, heater mass, gate-tip diameter) and are NOT covered; taper beyond 3°/side used in specialty foamed-material bushings; orifice sizing also depends on shot weight (Beaumont 2007 Table 6.2); measure nozzle radius with a radius gauge, worn nozzles deviate from nominal — `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/sprue_bushing_match.py`.

**MOLD-COOLING-TURBULENT-RE-CHECK** ✅ — `check_turbulent_re(CoolingFlowSpec) -> TurbulentReCheckReport` in `kerf_mold.cooling_turbulent_re_check`. Verifies cooling-channel Reynolds number Re = ρ·v·D/μ against the fully-turbulent threshold (Re ≥ 10 000) required for Dittus-Boelter correlation validity (Incropera & DeWitt eq. 8.60: Nu=0.023·Re^0.8·Pr^n). Flow-regime classification (White "Fluid Mechanics" §8.1): Re<2300 → "laminar" (AVOID — thermally stratified, very poor cooling), 2300≤Re<4000 → "transitional" (unpredictable; avoid), 4000≤Re<10000 → "turbulent" (Dittus-Boelter valid but h sub-optimal), Re≥10000 → "fully_turbulent" (target for mold cooling, Beaumont 2007 §11). Also computes minimum recommended flow rate [L/min] to reach Re=10000 for the given channel geometry and coolant. Dataclasses: `CoolingFlowSpec` (channel_diameter_mm, flow_rate_L_per_min, coolant_density_kg_m3=1000, coolant_viscosity_cP=1.0); `TurbulentReCheckReport` (reynolds_number, flow_regime, velocity_m_per_s, recommended_min_flow_rate_L_per_min, dittus_boelter_applicable, honest_caveat). Unit conversions: mm→m, L/min→m³/s÷60000, cP→Pa·s. LLM tool `mold_check_turbulent_re` registered in plugin.py; re-exported from `kerf_mold/__init__.py`. 24 tests green. **HONEST SCOPE: Re classification ONLY** — does NOT compute Nusselt number / convective HTC (requires Prandtl number input), polymer-side boundary layer, mold-steel wall thermal resistance, or part-steel contact resistance; does NOT model wall heat flux or non-uniform temperature distribution along the channel; single-phase, isothermal, incompressible, Newtonian fluid only (no two-phase/supercritical CO₂ cooling); viscosity spatially uniform (re-run with exit viscosity for ΔT > 10 °C); circular cross-section assumed (non-circular channels: supply hydraulic diameter D_h=4A/P) — `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/cooling_turbulent_re_check.py`. Refs: Beaumont 2007 §11 (cooling-system Re requirement); White "Fluid Mechanics" 8th ed. §8.1 (Re thresholds); Incropera & DeWitt "Heat and Mass Transfer" 7th ed. §8.5 eq. 8.60 (Dittus-Boelter Re≥10000).

**ARCH-BASE-PLATE-AISC (AISC DG-1 §3.1 + AISC 360-22 §J8)** ✅ — `design_base_plate(ColumnSpec, ConcreteSpec, Fy=345.0) -> BasePlateReport` implements steel column base plate design for concentric axial compressive loads. Concrete bearing strength: Pp = 0.85·f'c·A1·√(A2/A1) with A2/A1 ≤ 4 (AISC 360-22 §J8 Eq J8-2); φ_c = 0.65; required A1 = P_u/(φ_c·0.85·f'c·√(A2/A1)). Plate dimensions rounded up to nearest 5 mm; must cover column footprint (0.95·d × 0.80·bf per DG-1 §3.1.1). Cantilever arms: m=(N−0.95·d)/2 (Eq 3.1-1); n=(B−0.80·bf)/2 (Eq 3.1-2); n'=√(d·bf)/4; X=[4·d·bf/(d+bf)²]·[P_u/(φ_c·Pp)] (Eq 3.1-8); λ=min(1, 2·√X/(1+√(1−X))); l=max(m,n,λ·n'). Plate thickness via Murray-Stockwell (DG-1 Eq 3.1-5): t=l·√(2·P_u/(0.9·Fy·B·N)), rounded up to 1 mm. Oracle: W14x90, P=1000 kN, f'c=30 MPa, ped 600×600 mm → A1_req≈30166 mm²; plate 295×340 mm (column footprint governs, N_min=338 mm, B_min=295 mm); t=15 mm; DCR=0.318 (adequate). `arch_design_base_plate` LLM tool registered in plugin (gated import). Re-exported from arch/__init__.py. 24 hermetic oracle tests pass — `packages/kerf-cad-core/src/kerf_cad_core/arch/base_plate_aisc.py`. *SCOPE: concentric axial compressive load ONLY (DG-1 §3.1). NOT covered: moment transfer (DG-1 §3.2), anchor rod design (DG-1 §3.3–3.4), shear lug (DG-1 §3.5), biaxial bending, tensile uplift. A2 taken as pedestal plan area; irregular pedestals must supply equivalent rectangular A2. Grout strength ≥ f'c assumed.*

**Manufacturing depth** ✅ — **MOLD-COOLING-TIME-CHEN-CHIANG** (Chen-Chiang 1985 + Menges 2001 §7.3.3 + Beaumont 2007 §10.4): `compute_cooling_time_chen_chiang()` — 1-D Fourier first-term cooling-time formula: t_c = (h²/π²α)·ln[(8/π²)·(T_m−T_w)/(T_e−T_w)]; `MaterialThermalProps` dataclass (name, thermal_diffusivity_m2_per_s, T_melt_C, T_ejection_C); `CoolingTimeReport` dataclass (wall_thickness_mm, cooling_time_s, dominant_factor, material_used, honest_caveat); MATERIAL_THERMAL_DB (Menges 2001 Table 7.3): ABS α=1.00e-7, PC α=1.50e-7, PP α=0.95e-7, PA66 α=1.40e-7, POM α=0.95e-7, PMMA α=1.13e-7 m²/s; dominant-factor diagnosis (thickness_squared|diffusivity|temp_window) via log-sensitivity; LLM tool `mold_compute_cooling_time_chen_chiang` registered; 24 oracle tests; honest-flagged: 1-D Fourier first-term approximation only — ignores cooling-channel layout and conformal-cooling effects; does NOT model crystallisation latent heat (semi-crystalline PP/PA66/POM times 15–30% longer), thermal contact resistance, or hot-spot effects from varying wall thickness; use Moldflow/Moldex3D/SigmaSoft for a full cooling-circuit simulation — `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/cooling_time_chen_chiang.py` ✅.
**Manufacturing depth** ✅ — **MOLD-RUNNER-BALANCE-CHECK** (Beaumont 2007 §6.6 + Menges 2001 §6.6.4): `check_runner_balance()` — Hagen-Poiseuille hydraulic resistance path check for multi-cavity runner networks; R_norm = L/r⁴ per segment (μ cancels in ratios); path resistance summed sprue→gate via parent-pointer walk; max_imbalance_pct = 100×(R_max−R_min)/R_mean; balanced=True iff max_imbalance_pct < 5 % (Beaumont 2007 §6.6 criterion); `RunnerSegment` dataclass (id, length_mm, diameter_mm, parent_id); `RunnerBalanceReport` dataclass (cavity_paths[{cavity_id, total_length_mm, total_resistance, fill_ratio}], max_imbalance_pct, balanced, honest_caveat); LLM tool `mold_check_runner_balance` registered; 42 oracle tests; honest-flagged: geometric resistance only — does NOT model temperature-dependent or shear-thinning viscosity, shear-heating asymmetry in graduated-diameter (artificially balanced) runners (Beaumont RPI runner), or transient filling inertia; use Moldflow/Moldex3D/SigmaSoft for full rheological fill simulation — `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/runner_balance_check.py` ✅.
**Manufacturing depth** ✅ — mold draft-angle validation per face: arcsin(|n̂·pull̂|) draft angle; SPI finish grades A1–D3 minimum lookup (Menges 2001 §3.4 + Beaumont 2007 §4); region-aware minimums (outer 0.5°, inner 1.0°, rib 1.0°, boss 0.5°); top/bottom face pass-through; degenerate-normal flagging; LLM tool `mold_validate_draft`; 38 oracle tests; v1 honest-flag: undercut detection out of scope ✅.

**Manufacturing depth** ✅ — **MOLD-DRAFT-DEMOLD-FORCE** (Beaumont 2007 §9.3 + Menges 2001 §7.4 + Table 7.6): `compute_demold_force()` — cavity-ejection force per F = μ·σ_h·A·cosα/(cosα + μ·sinα); shrinkage stress σ_h from Menges Table 7.6 (ABS=4.0, PC=3.0, PP=5.0, PA66=3.5, POM=4.5 MPa); friction μ from SPI finish class (SPI_A1=0.15 polished … SPI_D1=0.40 textured); `MoldedPartSpec` dataclass (polymer_grade, contact_area_cm2, draft_angle_deg, mold_steel_finish_class); `DemoldForceReport` dataclass (demold_force_N, contact_pressure_MPa, ejector_pin_count_required, friction_coeff_used, polymer_shrinkage_stress_MPa, honest_caveat); ejector pin count = ceil(F / single_pin_capacity_N); LLM tool `mold_compute_demold_force` registered; 28 oracle tests; honest-flagged: empirical formula only — ignores chemical adhesion (resin stick, relevant for PC/POM on polished steel), undercut/side-action geometry, dynamic ejection force, and pin fatigue; confirm by mold-trial load-cell measurement — `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/demold_force_check.py` ✅.
**Manufacturing depth** ✅ — **MOLD-VENT-DEPTH-CHECK** (Beaumont 2007 §8.3 Table 8.2 + Menges 2001 §6.4 Table 6.7): `check_vent_depth()` — verify that a mold parting-line vent depth (air-escape gap) is within the polymer-specific recommended range; too shallow → trapped air → short shot / burn marks (diesel effect); too deep → flash; polymer database (mm): ABS 0.025–0.038, PC 0.013–0.025, PP 0.025–0.050, PA66 0.013–0.025, POM 0.013–0.025, PMMA 0.025–0.038, PE 0.038–0.075; `VentSpec` dataclass (polymer_grade, proposed_depth_mm, land_length_mm=1.5, vent_width_mm=6.0); `VentDepthReport` dataclass (recommended_depth_min_mm, recommended_depth_max_mm, compliant, depth_class, polymer_notes, honest_caveat); depth_class: "too_shallow"|"correct"|"too_deep"|"flash_risk" (>25% above max); unknown polymers receive fallback range [0.013–0.038 mm] with caveat; LLM tool `mold_check_vent_depth` registered; 35 oracle tests; honest-flagged: empirical handbook ranges only — actual safe vent depth depends on resin batch viscosity, melt temperature, injection speed, mold surface finish, land length, and part geometry; filled/FR/rubber-toughened grades may flash within the correct band for base resin; confirm by mold trial + visual flash inspection — `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/vent_depth_check.py` ✅.
**Manufacturing depth** ✅ — **MOLD-VENT-SLOT-LAYOUT** (Beaumont 2007 §8.5 Vent Slot Count and Width + Menges 2001 §6.4): `generate_vent_slot_layout()` — propose vent slot count, width (6 mm standard), and spacing for a parting-line perimeter given cavity volume, polymer grade, and injection speed; Beaumont 0.5 %-projected-area rule: total_vent_area ≥ 0.005 × cavity_volume_mm³/wall_thickness; speed scaling: vent_area_factor = max(1.0, injection_speed / 50 cm³/s); per-slot area = 6 mm width × depth_mid × 6 mm land length (polymer-specific depth from Beaumont Table 8.2); minimum 4 slots (one per quadrant, Beaumont §8.5; Menges §6.4); maximum slots = floor(perimeter / (6 + 10 mm steel bridge)); spacing = perimeter / n_slots; `MoldVolumeSpec` dataclass (cavity_volume_cm3, parting_line_perimeter_mm, polymer_grade, injection_speed_cm3_s); `VentSlotLayoutReport` dataclass (num_vent_slots, vent_slot_width_mm, vent_slot_spacing_mm, total_vent_width_mm, air_displacement_rate_cm3_s, adequate, honest_caveat); LLM tool `mold_generate_vent_slot_layout` registered; 47 oracle tests; honest-flagged: heuristic 0.5 %-area rule from production experience — NOT a first-principles fluid-dynamic calculation; wall thickness assumed 3 mm for area estimation; uniform spacing only (use mold_optimize_vent_placement for last-to-fill location optimisation); vent depth handled separately by mold_check_vent_depth; confirm by fill simulation (Moldflow / Moldex3D / SigmaSoft) + mold-trial visual inspection — `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/vent_slot_layout.py` ✅.
**Manufacturing depth** ✅ — **MOLD-RUNNER-COLD-SLUG** (Beaumont 2007 §6.7 Cold Slug Wells + Menges 2001 §6.5): `check_cold_slug_design()` — verify cold-slug well dimensions at runner junctions in a multi-cavity mold to trap the cold leading-edge polymer melt before it reaches the gate, preventing flow lines and weak weld lines; Beaumont rule: slug well diameter = 1.5 × runner diameter, depth = 2.0 × runner diameter, ±20 % tolerance band (1.2×–1.8× diameter, 1.6×–2.4× depth); `RunnerJunctionSpec` dataclass (junction_id, runner_diameter_mm, slug_well_diameter_mm, slug_well_depth_mm, polymer_grade); `ColdSlugReport` dataclass (junction_results list, total_junctions, compliant_count, honest_caveat); per-junction result: diameter_compliant, depth_compliant, slug_well_compliant, recommended_diameter_mm, recommended_depth_mm, tolerance bounds, reason; LLM tool `mold_check_cold_slug_design` registered; 32 oracle tests; honest-flagged: geometric rule-of-thumb only — actual cold-slug capture depends on melt temperature, injection speed, and resin freeze-off time; fast-crystallising resins (POM, PA66, LCP) and filled grades may require larger wells; confirm by mold trial + gate-area visual inspection; use Moldflow / Moldex3D / SigmaSoft for full melt-front thermal and weld-line simulation — `packages/kerf-mold/src/kerf_mold/cold_slug_check.py` ✅.

**Optics / acoustics** ✅ — Gaussian beam (complex-q + ABCD + M² + fibre coupling); non-sequential ray tracing + ghost detection; wave-domain room acoustics (image-source IR + Schroeder RT60 + SEA); Seidel S5 corrected; **Zernike polynomial wavefront fitting** (OPTICS-ZERNIKE-WAVEFRONT-FIT): first 15 Noll-ordered terms (j=1..15, piston through tetrafoil); explicit Z_j(ρ,θ) formulas (Noll 1976 Table 1 orthonormal basis); least-squares fit via numpy.linalg.lstsq; RMS residual; dominant aberration = argmax(|c_j|) for j≥2 (piston excluded); LLM tool `optics_fit_zernike_wavefront`; 32 hermetic tests. Am. 66 207; Born & Wolf §9.2; Wyant & Creath (1992).
**Optics / acoustics** ✅ — Gaussian beam (complex-q + ABCD + M² + fibre coupling); non-sequential ray tracing + ghost detection; wave-domain room acoustics (image-source IR + Schroeder RT60 + SEA); Seidel S5 corrected; **sequential paraxial + meridional ray trace** through multi-element lens stacks (Welford 1986 §3.3/§5, exact Snell + Newton-Raphson conic intersect; EFL/BFL/FFL; Hecht oracle biconvex BK7 <0.1% error; Cooke triplet converging verified); **MTF across field angle** (OPTICS-MTF-ACROSS-FIELD) — ray-bundle PSF histogram + numpy.fft.rfft pipeline; tangential MTF curves at multiple field angles; BK7 biconvex off-axis MTF drop verified; LLM tool `optics_mtf_across_field` (monochromatic; polychromatic MTF out of scope).

**Optics / acoustics** ✅ — **Chief-ray vignetting + relative illumination** (OPTICS-CHIEF-RAY-VIGNETTING): marginal-ray bundle traced at each field angle; per-surface clear-aperture clipping check; RI = surviving fraction; cos⁴(θ) photometric baseline; excess-vignetting ratio; LLM tool `optics_compute_vignetting` (Welford 1986 §4.5 / Hecht §6.6; circular symmetric apertures; 33 hermetic tests).
**Optics / acoustics** ✅ — **2-D relative illumination map** (OPTICS-RELATIVE-ILLUM-MAP): extends vignetting analysis to a full (grid × grid) heatmap across the image plane; for each (x, y) sensor position computes θ = arctan(r/EFL) and evaluates RI(θ) = surviving ray fraction via compute_vignetting; ri_map (aperture-clipping model) + cos4_map (natural cos⁴(θ) photometric baseline, Hecht §6.6 / Slyusarev §3.4); rotational-symmetry shortcut (1-D radial pre-computation, full 2-D output for visualisation); corner_ri + corner_cos4 diagnostics; BK7 biconvex @ sensor_half_height=60 mm → θ_corner ≈ 60°, cos4_corner ≈ 0.063; LLM tool `optics_compute_relative_illum_map`; 38 hermetic tests. **Optics / acoustics** ✅ — **Spot diagrams + pupil illumination maps** (OPTICS-PUPIL-DIAGRAM): uniform pupil-grid ray trace (Welford 1986 §8.2); per-field intercept loci at image plane; 2-D RMS + meridional y-only RMS spot radius; max ray distance from chief ray; exit-pupil illumination map (surviving pupil coords); paraxial exit-pupil position estimate (Welford 1986 §3.5 / Hecht §5.7); stigmatic stack → RMS < 1e-6 mm; BK7 biconvex at 14° → y-RMS > 3× on-axis; Seidel coma cross-check; LLM tool `optics_pupil_diagram` (monochromatic; sagittal x = first-order estimate; 33 hermetic tests).
**Optics / acoustics** ✅ — **Through-focus defocus curve** (OPTICS-DEFOCUS-CURVE): Welford 1986 §11.5 / Hecht §6.5; per-Δz meridional RMS spot-size via exact Snell + Newton-Raphson conic intersect; best-focus shift quantified; parabolic curve verified for paraxial singlet (min at Δz=0); spherical-aberration-shifted minimum verified for full-aperture BK7 singlet (Δz≈−0.5 mm); field-angle dependency; LLM tool `optics_defocus_curve`; 33 hermetic tests. Honest: monochromatic only; meridional (tangential) RMS only; astigmatic sagittal/tangential splitting not implemented.
**Optics / acoustics** ✅ — **Geometric distortion map** (OPTICS-DISTORTION-MAP): chief-ray tangential distortion vs field angle (Hecht §5.6 / Welford 1986 §6.3); D=(y_actual−y_paraxial)/|y_paraxial|×100; barrel (D<0) / pincushion (D>0) / mixed classification; Seidel S_V third-order cross-check (Welford §6.3); BK7 biconvex singlet shows measurable barrel distortion at moderate field (>0.5% at 20°); kind classification verified for high-power singlet and telephoto stacks; LLM tool `optics_distortion_map`; 30 hermetic tests. Honest: monochromatic only; tangential (meridional) distortion only; stop assumed at first surface.
**Optics / acoustics** ✅ — **Coma aberration metrics** (OPTICS-COMA-COMPUTE): comatic flare length from pupil-rim ray bundle trace (Welford 1986 §11.4 / Born & Wolf §5.3); for each field angle traces N marginal rays at entrance-pupil rim azimuths and propagates to paraxial focal plane; tangential coma = mean Y-displacement of tangential-fan rays from chief-ray image point; sagittal coma = tangential/3 (Welford §11.4 eq. 11.4.4); total coma = sqrt(tan²+sag²); Seidel S_II prediction = 3×|S_II|×|y_chief| (Born & Wolf §5.3 eq. 5.3.29); depth bar: BK7 biconvex at 14° → coma > 1 μm; Seidel match < 0.1% at 5° field; LLM tool `optics_compute_coma`; 33 hermetic tests. Honest: third-order coma only; higher-order (Hopkins 5th-order, oblique spherical aberration) requires finite-ray OPD analysis; monochromatic only; stop at first surface.
**Optics / acoustics** ✅ — **Seidel coma coefficient S_II** (OPTICS-SEIDEL-COMA): per-surface third-order Seidel coma sum S_II = Σ (−A_j·Ā_j·h_j·Δ(u/n)_j) via dual paraxial-ray trace (Welford 1986 §7 eq. 7.42 / Born & Wolf §5.3); SeidelComaReport dataclass: S_II (total Seidel coma sum), coma_waves_at_lambda (|3·S_II·y_chief|/(8λ)), dominant_surface_idx (argmax|S_II_j|), per_surface_contributions (A, Ā, h, ybar, delta_un, SII_contrib per surface), honest_caveat; BK7 biconvex R1=+50/R2=−50 mm on-axis → coma_waves = 0; same lens at 5° → S_II nonzero; aplanatic BK7+SF2 contact doublet → |S_II| reduced vs singlet; flat slab → S_II = 0 exactly; LLM tool `optics_compute_seidel_coma`; 34 hermetic tests. Honest: paraxial Seidel only; no chromatic coma; no defocus residual; stop at first surface; higher-order coma not modelled. Ref: Welford (1986) §7 eq. 7.42; Born & Wolf (1999) §5.3 eq. 5.3.29; Kingslake (1978).
**Optics / acoustics** ✅ — Gaussian beam (complex-q + ABCD + M² + fibre coupling); non-sequential ray tracing + ghost detection; wave-domain room acoustics (image-source IR + Schroeder RT60 + SEA); Seidel S5 corrected. **Longitudinal chromatic aberration** (OPTICS-CHROMATIC-FOCUS): Sellmeier dispersion n(λ) = sqrt(1 + Σ B_i λ²/(λ²−C_i)) for BK7/F2/SF6/K5/SF11/BK10 (Schott catalog 2023); per-wavelength BFL via ABCD thin-lens stack; LCA_FC = BFL(486nm)−BFL(656nm); Abbe V-number (singlet); BK7 V≈64.2 verified; achromat LCA < 0.1 mm verified; LLM tool `optics_compute_chromatic_focus`; 34 hermetic tests. Honest: paraxial thin-lens LCA only; chromatic lateral aberration not computed.
**Optics / acoustics** ✅ — **Abbe number + partial dispersion** (OPTICS-ABBE-NUMBER-COMPUTE): V_d = (n_d − 1) / (n_F − n_C) from Sellmeier Fraunhofer lines d/F/C (Hecht §6.3 / ISO 10110); secondary spectrum partial dispersion P_{F,g} = (n_g − n_F) / (n_F − n_C) for g-line (435.84 nm); six glasses BK7/F2/SF6/K5/SF11/BK10 (Schott 2023); BK7 V_d = 64.17, F2 = 36.37, SF6 = 25.43, K5 = 59.45, BK10 = 66.95 — all within 0.1% of catalog; SF11 = 25.37 (catalog 25.76, 1.5% gap documented — Sellmeier fit vs direct spectrophotometric measurement, Schott TIE-29 §3.3); LLM tool `optics_compute_abbe_number`; 30 hermetic tests. Honest: catalog nominal/melt-mean coefficients; melt-to-melt V_d variation ±0.3–0.5% (Schott TIE-31).

**Optics / acoustics** ✅ — **2-D relative illumination map** (OPTICS-RELATIVE-ILLUM-MAP): extends vignetting analysis to a full (grid × grid) heatmap across the image plane; for each (x, y) sensor position computes θ = arctan(r/EFL) and evaluates RI(θ) = surviving ray fraction via compute_vignetting; ri_map (aperture-clipping model: all 1.0 with no CA, drops with finite CAs) + cos4_map (natural cos⁴(θ) photometric baseline, Hecht §6.6 / Slyusarev §3.4); rotational-symmetry shortcut (1-D radial pre-computation, full 2-D output for visualisation); corner_ri + corner_cos4 diagnostics; BK7 biconvex @ sensor_half_height=60 mm → θ_corner ≈ 60°, cos4_corner ≈ 0.063; LLM tool `optics_compute_relative_illum_map`; 38 hermetic tests.
