- **Assembly mate inspector + validation** ✅ — validate joint geometries (concentric/coincident/distance/angle/tangent/parallel/perpendicular) between two B-rep bodies; residual + correction hints; auto-detect candidate mates by geometric similarity; full-assembly DOF accounting; `brep_validate_mate` + `brep_detect_mates` LLM tools; ASME Y14.5 §11 tolerance model. `packages/kerf-cad-core/src/kerf_cad_core/geom/mate_inspector.py`
- **Tolerance stack-up** ✅ — worst-case/RSS/Monte-Carlo + auto chain-walk.
- **GD&T frame validation (ASME Y14.5-2018)** ✅ — structural well-formedness per §3.4/§6/§9/§10/§12: symbol–modifier compatibility, datum requirements by tolerance category, duplicate-datum detection, bonus tolerance (MMC/LMC §6.3), canonical string round-trip; `gdt_validate_frame` + `gdt_parse_frame` LLM tools.
- **2D drawings** ✅ — multi-sheet, dimensions, GD&T frames, section hatching, leaders/balloons, centerlines.
- **3D PMI + GD&T annotation UI** ✅ — ISO 1101 GD&T toolbar (DrawingToolbar + GdntToolbar) with all 14 characteristics; datum A/B/C placement; FCF click-to-place modal with tolerance value, diameter zone, material-condition modifier, datum refs; SVG FCF glyphs (FcfGlyph/DatumGlyph) rendered inline per standard; 3D PMI overlay (Pmi3DOverlay) projects FCF labels into the three.js viewport; annotations persist via addFcf/addDatumLabel in the drawing data model.
- **Auto-dim ISO 129-1:2018** ✅ — chain / baseline / mixed dimensioning (§5.1); extension-line gap + overshoot (§5.4); 10 mm line spacing; leader lines at preferred 15° angles (§10); symmetric / unilateral / limit tolerance formats (§8); compliance validator; 2 LLM tools (`drawing_auto_dimension_iso`, `drawing_validate_iso`).
- **Auto 6-view + iso projection (ISO 128-30 / Bertoline 5e)** ✅ — `drawings/projections.py`: `generate_six_view_drawing` (front/back/top/bottom/left/right + iso); third-angle (ANSI/ASME Y14.3) and first-angle (ISO/DIN) layout; hidden-line removal per view via ray-cast depth test; `compute_projection_silhouette`; `drawing_auto_views` LLM tool; standard isometric 120° axis property validated (ISO 5456-3).
- **Section view auto-cutaway + ISO 128-30 hatch** ✅ — `cut_body_with_plane` + `hatch_cross_section` + `section_view_for_drawing`; marching-triangles half-body clipping; iron/concrete/plastic material hatch patterns; cutting-plane marker + Bertoline §11 arrow indicators; LLM tool `brep_section_view`.
- **Measurement chain auto-extraction (ASME Y14.5 + ISO 129)** ✅ — `extract_measurement_chain` generates a complete inspection dimension chain for a B-rep body: A/B/C datum-frame inference (§3.4), per-feature DOF coverage (holes: diameter + depth + 2 position dims), redundancy detection (ISO 129-1 §6 no-closed-chain rule), `generate_inspection_report` in ISO129 or ASME14.5 format; LLM tools `drawing_measurement_chain` + `drawing_inspection_report` wired.
- **2D drawings** ✅ — multi-sheet, dimensions, GD&T frames, section hatching, leaders/balloons, centerlines. NURBS silhouette projection to plane (Hertzmann 2000) ✅ — sign-change grid locus, NURBS curve fit, visible/hidden layer output.
- **NURBS surfacing (Phase 4)** ✅ — sweep1/2/network/blend/loft + `surface_continuity` (C0–C2/G0–G2); surface-direct boolean; trim-by-curve; curvature-comb viz; zebra/reflection-line viewport toggle. G3 *enforcement* on the OCCT side is structurally impossible (absent from OCCT's type system); pure-Python is the G3 path.
- **NURBS surfacing (Phase 4a — jewelry priority)** ✅ — `opSweep2` (two-rail sweep via `BRepFill_PipeShell`-style RMF midline, `sweep2_to_body` in `brep_build.py`), `opNetworkSrf` (Gordon/Coons-Gordon four-curve network, `network_srf_to_body`), `opBlendSrf` (G1/G2 Bezier blend strip, `blend_srf_to_body`); all three registered as LLM tools (`feature_sweep2`, `feature_network_srf`, `feature_blend_srf` in `surfacing.py`); 33 hermetic `validate_body`-clean tests in `test_phase4a_jewelry_surfacing.py`; scenario fixtures in `tests/fixtures/`.
- **Trim-loop auto-heal (T-junctions, dead loops, orientation)** ✅ — UV-domain repair pass: T-junction vertex merge (Sederberg-Zheng-Bakenov-Nasri 2003), dead-loop removal, CCW/CW orientation fix (Eberly shoelace), self-intersection detection; `nurbs_trim_loop_heal` LLM tool; 11 analytic-oracle tests.
- **NURBS seam control for periodic surfaces** ✅ — `detect_seam` / `shift_seam` / `align_seam_to_curve` in `geom/seam_control.py`; `nurbs_shift_seam` LLM tool registered; Piegl-Tiller §5.2 cyclic CP-net rotation with uniform knot rebuild; 16 analytic-oracle tests green.
- **Far-offset numerical conditioning** ✅ — `offset_far_correction.py` (Maekawa 1999 §6; Hoschek-Lasser 1993 §17): curvature-aware safety-distance computation (`safe_offset_distance`), adaptive local-refinement clamp (`offset_with_local_refinement`), graceful degradation with flagged unsafe parametric regions (`graceful_offset`); LLM tool `nurbs_surface_offset_robust` registered.
- **Variable-section extrude / morphing sweep** ✅ — `extrude_variable_section` (profile morphs per path parameter; linear / cubic-Hermite / C2 interpolation; Wang 2008 RMF frames) + `extrude_with_scaling_curve` (1-D scale taper along path) + `extrude_morph_via_rail_pair` (rail-guided profile morph); `nurbs_extrude_variable` LLM tool registered; 17 analytic-oracle tests green (constant-section degenerate, circle→square morph, conical-surface oracle, C2 smoothness).
- **NURBS curve/surface split at parameter** ✅ — `split_curve_at`, `split_curve_at_multiple`, `split_surface_at_u/v`; Piegl–Tiller §5.3 full-multiplicity knot insertion; rational-NURBS correct; LLM tools `nurbs_split_curve` + `nurbs_split_surface` registered (GK-P06).
- **Rhino parity** ✅ — 3DM I/O, SubD (Catmull-Clark), quad remesh, mesh tools, layers/display, parametric `.graph`, render output.
- **Persistent face naming** ✅ — sketch-anchored + topo-hash (frontend T1–T7) plus kernel-side `feature_id::role::fingerprint` selector in the pure-Python DAG.
- **Assembly interference detection (Möller 1997)** ✅ — `detect_interference_pair` / `detect_interference_assembly` / `compute_assembly_aabb`; AABB broad-phase + Möller 1997 triangle-triangle narrow phase + GK-18 boolean intersection volume; severity classification (none/touch/overlap/major_overlap); LLM tools `brep_assembly_interference` + `brep_check_clearance` — `kerf_cad_core/geom/assembly_interference.py`.

### Simulation / manufacturing

- **FEM** ✅ — FEniCSx + CalculiX: linear-static + modal + steady thermal + bonded contact; linear eigenvalue buckling + harmonic frequency response + random-vibration PSD; MITC4 plate/shell; acoustics FEM/BEM; high-frequency EM; electrostatics + magnetostatics; multi-axial fatigue; 2-D projection NS solver. Reference-value suite with Roark/Blevins/Incropera oracles (42 of 43 green).
- **CFD foundation** ✅ — 2-D laminar: potential flow (`Cp(θ)=1−4sin²θ` oracle) + lid-driven cavity (Ghia Re=100 reference); 61 hermetic tests.
- **Topology optimization** ✅ — SIMP via FEniCSx; NURBS surface fit; multi-body.
- **CAM** ✅ — 2.5D + 3D parallel/waterline + lathe + 5-axis constant-tilt + 3+2 indexed; tool DB; LinuxCNC/GRBL/Fanuc posts.
- **CAM toolpath collision verifier** ✅ — `cam_toolpath_collision.py`: segment-by-segment holder/spindle capsule-vs-AABB (Ericson 2005 §5.5) + capsule-vs-triangle-mesh (Möller 1997 §6) minimum-distance checks at 1 mm sampling resolution; configurable safety margin; fixture mesh support; `cam_verify_toolpath_collision` LLM tool. Known limit: worst-case missed gap ≤ step_mm × √2 ≈ 1.41 mm at default 1 mm step.
- **CAM feedrate lookahead optimizer** ✅ — `cam_feedrate_lookahead.py`: two-pass corner lookahead (Erkorkmaz-Altintas 2001 / Altintas 2012 §5.7); V_corner = sqrt(a_max × r_blend / sin(θ/2)); forward-pass acceleration + backward-pass deceleration; per-waypoint feedrate schedule + corner angles + cycle time. `cam_optimize_feedrate_lookahead` LLM tool. Honest limit: trapezoidal (constant-accel) profile only — jerk/S-curve not modelled.
- **5-axis CAM UI** ✅ — `CAMView.jsx` mode switch (3-axis / 5-axis-indexed / 5-axis-continuous); tilt axis (A/B/C) + angle; strategy (swarf / contour-on-tilted-plane / indexed-rough); spindle vector preview; dispatches `cam_run` backend tool (`operation=5axis_finish` or `3plus2`).
- **Feed-rate optimizer** ✅ — Altintas 2012 chip-load model + machine acceleration cap (§3.6) + tool deflection (Euler-Bernoulli); per-material/tool Vc+fz database (9 materials × 5 tool classes); forward–backward feed smoothing; MRR + cycle-time estimator. LLM tools: `manufacturing_optimize_feed`, `manufacturing_cycle_time`. (Altintas reference data — NOT cutting-tool-manufacturer-certified.)
- **MANUFACTURING-TOLERANCE-COST** ✅ — Tolerance-cost estimation (Boothroyd-Dewhurst §11.2 / Figure 11.4 exponential curve): `compute_tolerance_cost(tolerance_mm, process, base_cost_usd, dimension_mm)` → `ToleranceCostResult`; multiplier = exp(k × log10(t_max/t)); processes: turning (k=1.80, ±0.012–0.5 mm), milling (k=1.60, ±0.025–0.5 mm), grinding (k=2.50, ±0.002–0.02 mm), lapping (k=3.20, ±0.0005–0.005 mm); auto-upgrade chain (turning→grinding→lapping) when tolerance tightens beyond process capability; ISO 286-1:2010 IT-grade mapping (`tolerance_to_IT_grade`) for IT1–IT16; `manufacturing_tolerance_cost` LLM tool registered; 46 hermetic tests covering 4 tolerance bands × 2 processes, process-upgrade chain, IT-grade monotonicity, oracle B-D Fig 11.4 ratios, near-limit advisories, and LLM tool error paths. Honest-flag: simplified exponential fit; real cost depends on shop equipment, batch size, material hardness, and feature geometry — treat as ±30% estimate. References: Boothroyd-Dewhurst §11.2 + Fig 11.4 (2010); ASME B89.1.5-1998; ISO 286-1:2010 §4.
- **MANUFACTURING-MATERIAL-COST-ROLLUP** ✅ — Multi-cavity BOM material cost roll-up: `compute_material_cost_rollup(parts, material_db, waste_factor)` → `MaterialCostReport`; mass = volume_mm³ × density × 1e-6 [kg]; gross_mass = net × (1 + waste_factor); cost = gross_mass × price_per_kg; aggregation by material type, finishing operation, and cavity supplier; 2025 H1 spot-price baseline DB (LME + Plastics News) for 17 materials (ABS/PP/PC/PA66/PEEK/PLA/Al6061/Al7075/Steel304/316/1018/4140/Cu/Ti6Al4V/GrayIron/CFRP/GFRP); honest advisory: prices fluctuate — treat as H1 2025 baseline only; unknown materials zero-costed + flagged; `manufacturing_compute_material_cost_rollup` LLM tool; 26 oracle-asserted tests including Boothroyd-Dewhurst §8.3 depth-bar oracle (1000×ABS@100cm³ → $286.00 USD) and Al6061 cross-check — `kerf-cad-core/costing/material_cost_rollup.py` + `material_prices_2025.py`. References: Boothroyd-Dewhurst §8.3 (2010); ASME Y14.5-2018 §1.3; Tappi T 220 SP-08 (advisory).
- **3-2-1 Auto-fixture layout** ✅ — Asada-By (1985) §5 form-closure rank analysis; 6-locator placement (P1-P3 primary, P4-P5 secondary, P6 tertiary) on AABB workpiece; constraint matrix rank-6 validation; clamp-force estimates (material × operation); ASME B5.18-2018 compliant. `manufacturing_auto_fixture_layout` LLM tool.
- **CAM G-code emitter** ✅ — `cam_gcode_emit.py`: emit Fanuc-compatible RS-274 G-code from a waypoint toolpath (G00 rapid / G01 linear / G02 CW arc / G03 CCW arc / M03 spindle-on / M05 spindle-off / M06 tool change; I/J centre offsets; F feedrate modal; S spindle modal); `GcodeProgram` dataclass; `emit_gcode()` pure-Python function; `cam_emit_gcode` LLM tool. Round-trips through `parse_gcode`. Dialect: Fanuc 0i/18i/Haas/GRBL ≥ 1.1. Honest limit: XY-plane arcs only (G17); LinuxCNC %, Heidenhain TCPM, Siemens TRAORI out of scope. References: NIST RS-274/NGC (Kramer et al. 2000) §3.4–3.8; Smid CNC Programming Handbook (2008) §3. 44 tests.
- **CAM lathe profile G-code emitter** ✅ — `cam_lathe_profile.py`: emit complete Fanuc RS-274 lathe program from a 2-D axis-symmetric profile (XZ polyline); G71 rough turning cycle (P/Q/U/W/D/F/S words), G70 finish turning cycle, G96 constant surface speed, G97 constant RPM, M03/M05 spindle on/off, M06 tool change; `LatheProgram` dataclass; `emit_lathe_gcode(profile, stock, tool_id, sfm=600, ipr=0.25)` pure-Python; `cam_emit_lathe_gcode` LLM tool registered. Depth bar: cylinder Ø20→Ø10 step + tapered profile emit valid G71+G70 with stock allowance, 600 SFM steel, 0.25 mm/rev IPR; diameter programming (X = 2×radius); G18 ZX-plane preamble. Honest flag: Fanuc 0i-TF/30i dialect ONLY — Heidenhain TURN PLUS, Siemens ShopTurn CYCLE95, Mazak SmoothTurn, Okuma OSP lathe codes out of scope; G71 Type I only (monotone-decreasing X; concave features warned). References: NIST RS-274/NGC (Kramer et al. 2000) §3.4–3.9; Smid CNC Programming Handbook (2008) §6; Fanuc 0i-TF OM §14.2/14.3. 47 tests.
- **CAM wire-EDM path** ✅ — `cam_wire_edm_path.py`: Fanuc wire-EDM G-code from a 2-D profile (line + arc segments); G41/G42 cutter compensation (D-register = wire_radius + spark_gap; typical 0.135–0.150 mm); M50/M51 wire feed on/off; G01/G02/G03 with I/J; straight lead-in for safe compensation activation; `WireEDMProgram` dataclass; `square_profile` + `circle_profile` convenience builders; `cam_emit_wire_edm_gcode` LLM tool. Depth bar: 50×50 mm square → D=0.1500 mm (wire 0.25 mm, gap 0.025 mm); circle → G03 I/J=-25./I/J=+25.; all 46 tests green. Honest limits: 2-axis (XY) only — no wire taper (4-axis U/V), no threading hole automation, no skim passes, no variable-feed corners. Refs: Tlusty 2000 §13; Fanuc B-59064EN/01; Rajurkar et al. CIRP Annals 62(2):779-801.
- **CAM lead-in / lead-out arc segments** ✅ — `lead_in_out.py`: tangent-arc, line, and perpendicular lead-in/lead-out G-code segments for 2D contour milling; eliminates witness marks at cutter entry/exit (MH 31e §1131); `LeadSpec` + `LeadResult` dataclasses; `generate_lead_in_out(spec, cutter_comp)` — arc type: G02/G03 with I/J offsets (Fanuc incremental arc-centre convention), lead-in angle α (1–90°, 90° = classic perpendicular tangent entry), lead-in length = R·α_rad; line type: G01 approach along contour tangent; perpendicular type: G01 from normal offset; G41/G42 cutter compensation activated in lead-in block, G40 cancel in lead-out; `cam_generate_lead_in_out` LLM tool registered; 54 tests green. Honest limits: **2D contours only (XY plane, constant Z)** — 3D ramp entry and helical entry are NOT implemented; no gouge/collision checking (use `cam_verify_toolpath_collision`); I/J offsets are incremental/Fanuc convention (verify if using absolute arc-centre mode). Refs: MH 31e §1131; Fanuc Operator Manual §G41/G42.
- **CAM 3D parallel-offset surface milling** ✅ — `offset_3d_path.py`: `Offset3DSpec` + `Offset3DResult` + `generate_offset_3d_path(spec)` — raster (zig-zag parallel passes) toolpath at constant tool_radius Z-offset above a sampled z(x,y) surface grid; scallop height h = R − sqrt(R² − (ae/2)²) (Chuang & Yang 1995; Held & Klingenstein 1991 §3.1); bilinear z(x,y) interpolation; G21/G90/G94/M03/G00/G01/M05/M30 NIST RS-274/NGC §3.5 G-code; `cam_generate_offset_3d_path` LLM tool registered; 71 tests green. **Honest limits: 3-axis Z-axis-aligned only** (spindle always +Z vertical — no 5-axis tool-axis tilt; steep walls >45° receive slightly less than one tool_radius offset → potential micro-gouge on steep flanks per MH 31e §1139); **no gouge checking** (use `cam_verify_toolpath_collision`); **no z-level contouring / waterline passes** (raster only); no arc-fitting post-processor (all G01 linear segments); scallop formula is flat-surface approximation only (curved surface deviation not modelled). Time estimate constant-feed only (add 5–15 % per MH 31e §1109). Refs: MH 31e §1139 (3-axis surface offset); Held & Klingenstein (1991) Computers & Graphics 15(3):333–341; Chuang & Yang (1995) Intl J Mach Tools 35(2):261–267; NIST RS-274/NGC §3.5.
- **CAM-DRESS-CYCLE-WHEEL** ✅ — `dress_cycle.py`: `DressSpec` + `DressCycleResult` + `generate_dress_cycle(spec)` — open-loop grinding wheel dressing cycle G-code generator (traverse dressing); num_passes = ceil(total_dress_amount / depth_per_pass); per pass: G01 infeed X by depth_per_pass → G01 traverse Z across wheel_width at traverse_rate → G00 rapid-retract Z to start; G28 G91 Z0.0 reference return after final pass; G21/G90/G94/M05/M30 NIST RS-274/NGC preamble; `cam_generate_dress_cycle` LLM tool registered in plugin.py; 58 tests green. Dresser types: "single_point_diamond" (traverse 50–300 mm/min, depth 0.002–0.025 mm/pass) + "rotary_diamond" (traverse 100–800 mm/min, depth 0.005–0.050 mm/pass). HONEST: **open-loop only** — no in-process wheel diameter measurement or closed-loop correction (AE sensor, power monitoring, roundness gauging NOT implemented); uni-directional traverse only (+Z per pass, bi-directional oscillation NOT generated); no wheel-spindle synchronisation G-code for rotary roll speed; time estimate constant traverse + 3000 mm/min rapid Z retract only (acceleration ramps excluded, add 10–20%); G-code is RS-274/NGC / Fanuc 0i-PD compatible — controller-specific dress cycles (Siemens CYCLE12x, ANCA DressPro) NOT emitted; out-of-band advisory if traverse rate or depth outside MH 31e §1145 safe bands. Refs: MH 31e §1145 (Wheel dressing); Sandvik Coromant CoroGrind Grinding Handbook §5 (Wheel conditioning) — `packages/kerf-cam/src/kerf_cam/dress_cycle.py`.
- **CAM-MILLING-DWELL-CHECK** ✅ — `dwell_audit.py`: `DwellAuditSpec` + `DwellAuditReport` + `audit_milling_dwells(spec)` — G-code G04 dwell analysis for milling programs; parses every `G04 X<seconds>` (NIST RS-274/NGC §3.5) and `G04 P<ms>` (Fanuc/Haas) command; estimates G01 cutting time from line-by-line distance / modal feed rate (G94 mm/min); `total_dwell_time_ms`, `num_dwells`, `dwell_per_op_ms`, `total_program_time_estimate_s`, `dwell_ratio_pct`, `excessive` flag (ratio > `max_total_dwell_ratio_pct`, default 5 %), `suspicious_long_dwells` (> `max_recommended_dwell_per_op_ms`, default 500 ms); modal G20/G21, G90/G91, G94/G95 state tracked; `cam_audit_milling_dwells` LLM tool registered; 45 tests green. HONEST: heuristic only — some dwells are deliberate (G89 boring spindle-settle, machine warm-up, coolant-pressure build); `excessive=True` is NOT proof of a programming error; G02/G03 arc moves excluded from cutting-time estimate (inflates dwell_ratio_pct for arc-heavy programs); G95 feed-per-rev blocks contribute 0 to cutting time; rapid rate assumed 10 000 mm/min (generic constant); acceleration ramps add 15–30 % to wall-clock time (Altintas 2012 §5.7). Refs: MH 31e §1140 (Dwell commands); NIST RS-274/NGC §3.5 — `packages/kerf-cam/src/kerf_cam/dwell_audit.py`.
- **CAM-MILL-PROFILE-ROUGHING** ✅ — `profile_roughing.py`: `ProfileMillSpec` + `ProfileRoughingResult` + `generate_profile_roughing(spec)` — multi-pass 2D profile roughing toolpath that progressively removes material from a closed CCW polygon boundary with adjustable stock offset, leaving a finish allowance for the final pass. Strategy: `num_axial = ceil(total_depth / depth_per_pass)` axial levels; per level, successive radial inward passes from `stock_offset_mm` down to `finish_allowance_mm` (step = cutter_radius = D/2 per pass, outermost → finish-spring pass); polygon offset via vertex bisector / Minkowski-sum approximation (Preparata & Shamos 1985 §8.4); G21/G90/G94/M03/G00/G01/M05/M30 NIST RS-274/NGC §3.5 G-code; `cam_generate_profile_roughing` LLM tool registered; 76 tests green. HONEST: **2D polygon profile only** — no pocket-with-islands (island/internal boundaries not supported); no climb/conventional milling differentiation (all passes use same direction); no helical or ramping entry (plunges at feed rate); no cutter compensation G41/G42 (offsets pre-computed in software); polygon offset is bisector approximation — exact for convex profiles, may self-intersect on highly non-convex geometries (use Clipper library for production); time estimate constant-feed only (add 5–15 % per MH 31e §1109). MRR = (stock_polygon_area − finish_polygon_area) × total_depth. Refs: MH 31e §1131 (profile milling); Sandvik CoroPlus Contour Roughing (2024); NIST RS-274/NGC §3.5 — `packages/kerf-cam/src/kerf_cam/profile_roughing.py`.
- **CAM-COOLANT-FLOW-CHECK** ✅ — `coolant_flow_check.py`: `MachiningOpForCoolant` + `CoolantFlowReport` + `check_coolant_flow(spec)` — recommends minimum coolant flow rate [L/min] and pressure [bar] for a CNC machining operation; verifies whether the spindle/through-tool coolant system can deliver them. Flow heuristic: `required_flow = flow_factor × MRR`; material factors (Sandvik CoroPlus §3): steel=0.50, stainless=0.60, aluminum=0.30, titanium=0.50, composite=0.20 L/min per cm³/min. Pressure thresholds (Sandvik CoroPlus §3): titanium any coolant ≥70 bar; through-tool d>8mm ≥20 bar; through-tool d≤8mm ≥10 bar; flood ≥2 bar; mist ≥4 bar; MQL ≥5 bar. Material-specific recommended coolant type: titanium → through_tool (mandatory high-pressure); stainless → through_tool (chip-breaking + heat); steel → flood; aluminum → flood; composite → MQL. `cam_check_coolant_flow` LLM tool registered in plugin.py; 41 tests green. HONEST: flow factors are heuristic averages — actual requirements depend on ae/ap ratio, specific alloy thermal conductivity, insert grade, and chip volume; coolant chemistry (concentration, pH, biocide), chip-evacuation effectiveness, and nozzle positioning are NOT modelled; high-pressure through-tool channels require spindle + toolholder physically rated for that pressure (seal integrity not checked); MQL/mist flow is lubricant volumetric flow, not flood coolant; composite CFRP/GFRP may require dry or MQL-only machining regardless of flow rate. Refs: Sandvik CoroPlus Coolant Application Guide §3 (2024); MH 31e §1140 (Coolant application) — `packages/kerf-cam/src/kerf_cam/coolant_flow_check.py`.
- **CAM chip-load + chip-thinning calculator** ✅ — `chip_load_calc.py`: `MillingOpSpec` + `ChipLoadReport` + `compute_chip_load(spec)` — fz = Vf/(n×z) (MH 31e §1136); radial chip-thinning Krad = D/(2·sqrt(D·ae − ae²)) when ae < D/2 else 1.0 (Sandvik CoroPlus 2024; Stephenson-Agapiou §6); actual_chip_load = fz × Krad; MRR = ae × ap × Vf / 1000 cm³/min; Sandvik CoroPlus 2024 recommended fz ranges (carbide/aluminium 0.05–0.15, carbide/steel 0.05–0.20, HSS/aluminium 0.03–0.10, HSS/steel 0.03–0.12, ceramic 0.10–0.30 mm/tooth); compliant flag; work_material lookup supports aluminium/aluminum/steel/stainless_303/aluminum_6061; `cam_compute_chip_load` LLM tool registered; 32 tests green. Honest caveats: thinning formula assumes circular arc-of-engagement (flat workpiece, peripheral end-mill only) — ball-nose tools, curved workpieces, profiling passes change engagement geometry; no climb/conventional distinction (both use same Krad); tool deflection NOT modelled (see Altintas 2012 §3.6); recommended ranges are material-class averages — verify against CoroPlus ToolGuide for production. References: MH 31e §1136; Sandvik CoroPlus Milling/feed-per-tooth (2024); Stephenson-Agapiou §6.
- **CAM-DEEP-PECK-LIVE-TIME** ✅ — `peck_live_time.py`: `PeckCycleParams` + `PeckLiveTimeReport` + `compute_peck_live_time(params)` — G83 peck-drill cycle live-time analytics: num_pecks = ceil(depth/peck_depth); per-peck model: rapid-down from R-plane to current bore top + feed drilling stroke + rapid-up to R-plane + optional dwell; live_time_fraction = cutting_s / total_cycle_s; adequate flag (threshold 0.50 per Sandvik CoroPlus 2024); separates cutting / retract / dwell times; `cam_compute_peck_live_time` LLM tool registered; 52 tests green. Use: chip-evacuation analysis (low live fraction → heat cycling → accelerated tool wear); tool-life budgeting (cutting-second accounting). Honest caveats: **ideal rigid rapid assumed** — no acceleration ramps at peck reversal (real machines add 5–20 % retract overhead per Sandvik CoroPlus 2024 §Annex C servo dynamics); full-retract G83 per NIST RS-274/NGC §3.8.4 — partial-retract G73/Haas-chip-break controllers will yield higher actual live fractions; dwell reported separately (not charged to cutting or retract). References: MH 31e §1132; Sandvik CoroPlus Drill Cycle Analytics (2024); NIST RS-274/NGC §3.8.4.
- **CAM** ✅ — 2.5D + 3D parallel/waterline + lathe + 5-axis constant-tilt + 3+2 indexed; tool DB; LinuxCNC/GRBL/Fanuc posts; G83 peck-drilling canned cycle (NIST RS-274/NGC §3.8.4); G84/G74 rigid tapping canned cycle (NIST RS-274/NGC §3.8.4 + MH 31e §1934; `cam_generate_tap_cycle` LLM tool; honest caveat: rigid tap timing only — floating tap holders not modelled); G85/G86/G89 boring canned cycles (NIST RS-274/NGC §3.8.4 + MH 31e §1162; `cam_generate_boring_cycle` LLM tool; G85=feed-out Ra 0.8 μm, G86=spindle-stop-out Ra 1.6 μm, G89=dwell-out Ra 0.4 μm; honest caveat: single-point boring bar only — no roughing/finishing pass differentiation; G89 P-word in μs per NIST vs ms Fanuc); **zig-zag face-mill toolpath** (`face_mill_path.py`): `FaceMillSpec` + `FaceMillResult` + `generate_face_mill_path(spec, climb_milling=True)` — rectangular pocket bbox + tool diameter + 70 % stepover (MH 31e §1136) → full G21/G90/G94/M03/G00/G01/M30 NIST RS-274/NGC §3.5 G-code; climb vs conventional milling; `cam_generate_face_mill_path` LLM tool; 71 tests. Honest limits: 2.5D only (single flat depth); no helical entry; no cutter comp G41/G42; no high-feed (HFC) strategies; no corner arcs at pass reversal; time estimate excludes acceleration ramps (add 5–15 %, MH 31e §1109). **Rigid-tap pre-run check** (`rigid_tapping_check.py`): `RigidTapSpec` + `RigidTapReport` + `check_rigid_tap(spec)` — validates a rigid-tap operation against machine spindle synchronisation capability and tap-strength limits; torque T = K·D³ (Sandvik CoroPlus 2024 + MH 31e §1934 empirical K coefficients: HSS-steel=0.35, cobalt-steel=0.30, carbide-steel=0.25, HSS-aluminum=0.10; 4 materials × 3 tool classes); feed F = pitch × rpm; sync_compliant = rpm ≤ machine_max_sync_rpm; tap_breakage_risk (low/medium/high) heuristic: deep hole (>3×D), rpm above material/tool limit, stainless+small+HSS combo; recommended_feed_override_pct; metric (M6x1.0, M10x1.5) + inch UNC/UNF (1/4-20, 3/8-16) thread parser; `cam_check_rigid_tap` LLM tool registered; 58 tests green. Honest caveat: K coefficients ±35 % — coolant effects, tap geometry (spiral-flute vs spiral-point), thread-fit class, and worn tool state NOT modelled. References: Sandvik CoroPlus Technical Guide 2024; MH 31e §1934; NIST RS-274/NGC §3.8.4.
- **Slicing** ✅ — plane-section, CNC layered, 3D-print G-code (Cura, Tier 1).
- **HVAC duct pressure loss — ASHRAE §35 fittings** ✅ — ASHRAE Handbook of Fundamentals 2021 §35 (Ch. 21) Table 21-1 fitting loss coefficients: 10 fitting kinds (smooth/segmented elbows, 45° elbow, tee branch/through, gradual/abrupt transitions, butterfly damper, gradual reducer/expander); `fitting_pressure_loss()` + `compute_duct_run_pressure_drop()` (straight-duct + fittings combined); `build_loss_table()` with full ASHRAE citations; 2 new LLM tools (`hvac.fitting_pressure_loss`, `hvac.compute_run_pressure_drop`).
- **Slicing** ✅ — plane-section, CNC layered, 3D-print G-code (Cura, Tier 1); infill pattern library (gyroid TPMS, honeycomb, triangular grid, concentric) ✅.
- **1D system simulation (kerf-1dsim)** ✅ — Modelica-compatible equation-based DAE solver (BDF-1); R/L/C/MassSpring/Damper/ThermalConductor/FluidResistor components; **Modelica .mo import** ✅ — recursive-descent subset parser: `model/end`, `parameter Real`, `Real`, `equation`, `der()`, `connect()`, `package` wrapping; `modelica_to_kerf_components` mapper; `load_modelica_library` directory scan; `sim_import_modelica` LLM tool registered. *Modelica subset support — NOT certified Modelica compliance.*
- **1DSim** ✅ — Modelica-compatible equation-based DAE solver (BDF-1); Modelica import; FMI export; **SPICE 3F5 netlist import + MNA DC analysis** (R/C/L/V/I/Q/M parsing, `sim_import_spice` + `sim_dc_analysis` LLM tools; SPICE subset — NOT SPICE-certified, BSIM models out of scope).

T-225..T-230.
- **FIRMWARE-PERIPHERAL-MAP-VERIFY** ✅ — peripheral pin-mapping verifier against MCU hardware alt-function tables; detects: bad alt-function, pin conflict, missing required, peripheral pin-mux conflict, voltage incompatibility (5V tolerant check); embedded STM32F411 LQFP64 alt-function table (RM0383 §7.3, PA0..PC15) + ATmega328P PDIP-28 (datasheet §13, all 23 GPIOs); `firmware_verify_peripheral_map` LLM tool; `chip_specs.py` + `peripheral_map_verify.py`; 59 tests. NOT a substitute for ST CubeMX / Atmel Start.
- **Silicon / IC layout** ✅ — VHDL + Verilog parsers; GHDL + Yosys + ngspice bridges; GDS II / OASIS I/O; SKY130 PDK; LEF/Liberty readers; OpenROAD place-and-route; DRC + LVS + parasitic extraction; mask fracturing; SPICE waveform viewer UI ✅. T-231..T-248.
- **Silicon / IBIS 7.1 signal integrity** ✅ — IBIS 7.1 model import + eye-diagram estimation (`silicon_import_ibis`, `silicon_eye_diagram`); [Component]/[Pin]/[Model]/[Pulldown]/[Pullup]/[GND_clamp]/[POWER_clamp]/[Ramp]/[Voltage Range]; IV-curve interpolation; analytical eye opening height/width/jitter at arbitrary bit-rate + load. NOT IBIS-certified.
- **Firmware / embedded** ✅ — board catalogue (Arduino/ESP32/STM32/RP2040/AVR); library cache; direct-gcc orchestrator (`avr-gcc`/`arm-none-eabi-gcc`/`xtensa-esp32-elf`); upload wrappers; serial monitor panel; LLM tools. T-225..T-230.
- **FIRMWARE-PERIPHERAL-MAP-VERIFY** ✅ — peripheral pin-mapping verifier; detects bad alt-function, pin conflict, missing required, peripheral mux conflict, voltage incompatibility; embedded STM32F411 LQFP64 (RM0383 §7.3) + ATmega328P PDIP-28 tables; `firmware_verify_peripheral_map` LLM tool; 59 tests.
- **FIRMWARE-CLOCK-TREE-VERIFY** ✅ — STM32 clock-tree verifier; real PLL arithmetic (VCO = HSE/PLLM × PLLN; SYSCLK = VCO/PLLP; USB = VCO/PLLQ); detects VCO out of range, SYSCLK exceeded (100 MHz F411 / 168 MHz F407), APB1 > 42 MHz, APB2 > 84 MHz, USB ≠ 48 MHz (±500 ppm), ADC > 36 MHz; embedded RM0383 §6 (STM32F411) + RM0090 §6 (STM32F407) tables; `firmware_verify_clock_tree` LLM tool; `clock_tree_specs.py` + `clock_tree_verify.py`; 71 tests. LOOKUP-TABLE ONLY — no jitter/phase-noise model.
- **FIRMWARE-DMA-CHANNEL-CONFLICT** ✅ — STM32 DMA controller channel-assignment verifier; detects: INVALID_ASSIGNMENT (peripheral not legal on stream/channel, with alternatives), STREAM_CONFLICT (two peripherals on same stream), UNKNOWN_CONTROLLER; embedded RM0383 §10.3.3 Tables 27–28 (STM32F411) + RM0090 §10.3.3 Tables 42–43 (STM32F407) stream-channel-peripheral matrices; `firmware_verify_dma_assignments` LLM tool; `dma_specs.py` + `dma_channel_conflict.py`; 64 tests. STATIC CONFLICT DETECTION ONLY — no DMA throughput/priority/FIFO model.
- **FIRMWARE-INTERRUPT-PRIORITY-VERIFY** ✅ — Cortex-M NVIC interrupt priority verifier; detects: OUT_OF_RANGE (priority outside [0,15] for STM32F4xx 4-bit field), SAME_PREEMPT_PRIORITY (two peripherals share a preemption level — non-deterministic tie-break by IRQ number, ARM Cortex-M Generic UG §B3.3), RT_IN_LOW_BAND (TIM/EXTI in LOW band, pre-empted by NORMAL), NON_RT_IN_RT_BAND (USB/ADC/RTC in RT band), UNKNOWN_PERIPHERAL, BASEPRI_MISCONFIGURED (BASEPRI=0 disables masking, §B1.5.4); PRIGROUP-aware preemption-level extraction (CMSIS NVIC_EncodePriority formula); embedded RM0383 Rev 3 §10 STM32F411 + RM0090 Rev 19 §10 STM32F407 IRQ tables; `firmware_verify_interrupt_priorities` LLM tool; `interrupt_specs.py` + `interrupt_priority_verify.py`; 93 tests. STATIC CHECKS ONLY — no WCET, RTOS priority-inheritance, or runtime latency model.
- **FIRMWARE-MEMORY-MAP-VERIFY** ✅ — Cortex-M linker memory-layout verifier; detects: FLASH_OVERFLOW (sections exceed chip Flash capacity, RM0383 §3), SRAM_OVERFLOW (runtime sections exceed chip SRAM capacity), STACK_OVERFLOW_INTO_BSS (stack + .data + .bss > SRAM; conservative static check), VECTOR_TABLE_MISPLACED (vector table base not at Flash start and not in SRAM for VTOR remap, ARM Cortex-M Generic UG §B3.2.4), ISR_COUNT_MISMATCH (vector table entry count != chip NVIC count, RM0383 §10); embedded memory maps for STM32F411 (512 KB Flash / 128 KB SRAM, RM0383 §3) + STM32F407 (1 MB Flash / 128 KB SRAM, RM0090 §3); `firmware_verify_memory_map` LLM tool; `memory_map_verify.py`; 63 tests. STATIC SECTION-SIZE CHECK ONLY — does not run the linker; use arm-none-eabi-size + map-file for production audits.
- **FIRMWARE-SPI-TIMING-VERIFY** ✅ — SPI master/slave timing compatibility verifier; checks: master clock_hz ≤ slave max_clk_hz, master setup_ns ≥ slave min_setup_ns, master hold_ns ≥ slave min_hold_ns, CPOL exact match, CPHA exact match (Motorola SPI spec canonical CPOL/CPHA definition + ARM Cortex-M Generic UG §SPI Timing); reports clock_margin_pct, setup_margin_ns, hold_margin_ns, violation list; violation codes: CLOCK_TOO_FAST, SETUP_VIOLATION, HOLD_VIOLATION, CPOL_MISMATCH, CPHA_MISMATCH; edge case: MCP3008 ADC at 1.35 MHz max (DS21295D §1.0 Table 1-1) verified against STM32F411 SPI1 @ 1 MHz; `firmware_verify_spi_timing` LLM tool; `spi_timing_verify.py`; 41 tests. HONEST: assumes ideal square-wave signals; ignores PCB trace propagation delay and crosstalk; use a logic analyser on real hardware.
- **FIRMWARE-I2C-CLOCK-STRETCH-CHECK** ✅ — I²C clock-stretch worst-case effective speed analyser; computes effective I²C bus frequency when slaves exercise SCL clock stretching and verifies SCL low-timeout compliance; algorithm per NXP UM10204 Rev 7 §3.1.9: t_byte_effective = (9/f_nom) + stretch_us/1e6; f_effective = 9/t_byte_effective; timeout_compliant = (worst_stretch_us × bytes_per_txn) < scl_low_timeout_ms×1000; reports effective_clock_hz, worst_case_stretch_per_byte_us, timeout_compliant, slowest_slave, throughput_degradation_pct; `firmware_check_i2c_clock_stretch` LLM tool; `i2c_clock_stretch_check.py`; 36 tests. HONEST: assumes synchronous single-master bus — multi-master arbitration NOT modelled; stretch accumulated conservatively on every byte; rise/fall derating and t_BUF overhead not included; verify on target hardware with a logic analyser. Refs: NXP UM10204 Rev 7 §3.1.9; STM32F411 RM0383 §26.6 TIMEOUTB register.
- **FIRMWARE-UART-BAUD-DRIFT-CHECK** ✅ — UART baud-rate drift analyser; given MCU clock (Hz) and UBRR divisor register value, computes actual baud rate and percent drift vs nominal; flags unreliable links (|drift| ≥ 2%, per RS-232 / IEEE Std 488 baud-rate tolerance); recommends closest standard baud + UBRR combinations that achieve < 0.5% drift with the same clock; ATmega normal mode: baud = clock / (16×(UBRR+1)); double_speed (U2X): baud = clock / (8×(UBRR+1)); standard bauds: [9600, 19200, 38400, 57600, 115200, 230400, 460800, 921600]; `UartConfigSpec` + `BaudDriftReport` dataclasses; `check_uart_baud_drift` function; `firmware_check_uart_baud_drift` LLM tool; `uart_baud_drift_check.py`; 24 tests. HONEST: ATmega integer-divisor model is exact for AVR; for STM32 (fractional BRR register, RM0383 §19) this model OVER-ESTIMATES drift — the STM32 fractional generator typically achieves < 0.1% on standard bauds whereas this integer model reports ~0.94% at 80 MHz / 115200; clock-source tolerance (crystal ±100 ppm, resonator ±0.5%) not modelled; verify on target hardware with oscilloscope or logic analyser. Refs: ATmega328P §19 (USART); STM32F411 RM0383 §19; IEEE Std 488.
- **FIRMWARE-FLASH-WEAR-LEVEL** ✅ — MCU flash endurance and time-to-failure estimator for EEPROM-like wear-leveling; given sector layout, write rate, and N-sector wear-leveling pool: total_writes = writes_per_second × 31,557,600 s/yr × lifetime_years; sector_erase_events = ceil(total_writes / ceil(sector_size / bytes_per_write)); cycles_per_sector = sector_erase_events / N; adequate = cycles_per_sector ≤ endurance_cycles; time_to_failure_years = endurance × N × WA / writes_per_sec / sec_per_yr; recommended_sectors = ceil(sector_erases / endurance); depth-bar: STM32F411 128 KB sector (RM0383 §3, 10k cycles), 1 write/s, 10 yr, 1 sector → 3.15e8 cycles (31,558× over limit, need ~31,558 sectors); same with 100 sectors → 3.15e6 (still 316× over limit); ATmega328P EEPROM (§11, 100k cycles), 0.0001 write/s, 10 yr → 31,558 cycles → adequate; `FlashSpec` + `WriteWorkload` + `FlashWearReport` dataclasses; `compute_flash_wear` function; `firmware_compute_flash_wear` LLM tool; `flash_wear_level.py`; 26 tests. HONEST: assumes perfect uniform wear distribution — real algorithms (NuttX MTD, Zephyr NVS, ST EEPROM emulation AN2594) achieve ~80–90% of ideal; divide time_to_failure_years by 0.85 for conservative estimate; write amplification is worst-case (one sector erase per logical write); streaming / buffered writes achieve lower WA; temperature derating not modelled (STM32F411 endurance halves at Tj = 125°C per RM0383 §3 Table 6). Refs: STM32F411 RM0383 §3; ATmega328P §11; JEDEC JESD47 §9.
- **FIRMWARE-FLASH-WEAR-LEVEL** ✅ — MCU flash endurance and time-to-failure estimator for EEPROM-like wear-leveling; total_writes = writes_per_second × 31,557,600 s/yr × lifetime_years; cycles_per_sector = ceil(total_writes / WA) / N; adequate = cycles_per_sector ≤ endurance_cycles; recommended_sectors = ceil(sector_erases / endurance); depth-bar: STM32F411 128 KB sector (RM0383 §3, 10k cycles), 1 write/s, 10 yr, 1 sector → 3.15e8 cycles (inadequate); ATmega328P EEPROM (§11, 100k cycles), 0.0001 write/s, 10 yr → 31,558 cycles (adequate); `FlashSpec` + `WriteWorkload` + `FlashWearReport` dataclasses; `compute_flash_wear` function; `firmware_compute_flash_wear` LLM tool; `flash_wear_level.py`; 26 tests. HONEST: assumes perfect uniform wear distribution — real algorithms (NuttX MTD, Zephyr NVS, ST AN2594) achieve ~80–90% of ideal; WA model is worst-case; temperature derating not modelled. Refs: STM32F411 RM0383 §3; ATmega328P §11; JEDEC JESD47 §9.
- **FIRMWARE-RAM-USAGE-AUDIT** ✅ — MCU RAM utilisation auditor; given .data (initialised globals), .bss (zero-inited globals), heap_max_bytes (worst-case dynamic allocation estimate), stack_max_bytes (worst-case stack depth estimate), and total_ram_bytes: static_alloc = data + bss; dynamic_alloc = heap + stack; total_used = static_alloc + dynamic_alloc; free_bytes = max(0, total_ram − total_used); utilization_pct = total_used / total_ram × 100; within_budget = total_used ≤ 80% of total_ram (10% safety guard for interrupt frames + malloc metadata); recommendation identifies largest contributor when over budget; depth-bar: STM32F411 128 KB (RM0383 §2) data=8KB/bss=16KB/heap=24KB/stack=8KB → 56 KB used, 72 KB free, 43.75% util → adequate; ATmega328P 2 KB (§8) data=500B/bss=1200B/heap=200B/stack=100B → 2000 B used, 48 B free, 97.66% → over budget; `MemorySectionSizes` + `RamUsageReport` dataclasses; `audit_ram_usage` function; `firmware_audit_ram_usage` LLM tool; `ram_usage_audit.py`; 46 tests. HONEST: static estimate only — does not account for malloc fragmentation (budget 20–30% overhead for general-purpose allocators) or interrupt-driven stack growth (each Cortex-M interrupt frame = 32 B; nested ISRs multiply this); RTOS task stacks not counted unless included in heap_max_bytes / stack_max_bytes; validate stack peak with stack-painting or RTOS uxTaskGetStackHighWaterMark(). Refs: RM0383 Rev 3 §2 (STM32F411 SRAM map); ATmega328P §8 (SRAM organisation).
- **FIRMWARE-STACK-DEPTH-ESTIMATE** ✅ — static worst-case stack depth estimator for Cortex-M / ATmega firmware; DFS through the function call graph accumulating per-function frame sizes; detects recursive cycles (back-edges); adds ISR preemption overhead once (default 32 B = Cortex-M3/M4/M7 exception frame: 8 registers × 4 B, ARM Cortex-M Generic UG §B1.5.6); depth-bar: main(100 B) → A(200 B) → B(50 B) + ISR 32 B = 382 B total; cycle A→B→A flagged as has_cycles=True; ATmega variant passes isr_overhead_bytes=3 (PC save only); multiple-callee branching takes deepest path; `FunctionFrame` + `StackDepthReport` dataclasses; `estimate_stack_depth` function; `firmware_estimate_stack_depth` LLM tool; `stack_depth_estimate.py`; 38 tests. HONEST: STATIC ESTIMATE ONLY — does not account for VLA (variable-length arrays; makes exact depth undecidable), alloca(), longjmp/setjmp, or indirect calls (function pointers, callbacks); frame sizes must come from arm-none-eabi-gcc / avr-gcc -fstack-usage (*.su files), not guesses; RTOS tasks each have their own stack — analyse each task independently; recursive cycles report a per-iteration lower bound only. Refs: ARM IHI 0042F AAPCS §5.2/§6.1; ARM Cortex-M Generic UG §B1.5.6; Greenwood (2011) "Static Stack Analysis for Embedded Systems" §3; Brylow et al. (2001) LCTES/OM.
- **FIRMWARE-RTOS-PRIORITY-CHECK** ✅ — FreeRTOS / Zephyr / ChibiOS task priority assignment verifier; Liu-Layland (1973) rate-monotonic schedulability bound: U = Σ Cᵢ/Tᵢ ≤ n·(2^(1/n)−1); also evaluates Bini-Buttazzo (2001) tighter hyperbolic bound Π(Uᵢ+1) ≤ 2; verifies RM priority assignment (shorter period → higher priority integer, FreeRTOS/Zephyr/ChibiOS convention); depth-bar: 2 tasks T1 period=10ms WCET=4ms (P2), T2 period=20ms WCET=8ms (P1) → U=80%, bound=82.84%, schedulable, assignment correct; overload detection with recommendation to reduce WCET or lengthen periods; high-utilisation (>90%) headroom warning; largest contributor advisory; `RtosTaskSpec` + `RtosPriorityReport` dataclasses; `check_rtos_priorities` function; `firmware_check_rtos_priorities` LLM tool; `rtos_priority_check.py`; 43 tests. HONEST: sufficient condition only for independent periodic tasks — does NOT model shared resources (PCP/PIP, requires Sha-Rajkumar-Lehoczky 1990 blocking-time response-time analysis), aperiodic/sporadic tasks (Deferrable/Sporadic Server algorithms), interrupt latency, context-switch overhead, or deadlines ≠ periods (use EDF/DM for Dᵢ ≠ Tᵢ). Refs: Liu-Layland (1973) J. ACM 20(1); Bini-Buttazzo (2001) ECRTS; ARM FreeRTOS Kernel Developer Docs; Renesas R01AN5545; Zephyr Scheduling Docs.

## In flight

| # | What | Why it matters | Status |
|---|---|---|---|
| **P0-5** | **Large-assembly performance ceiling** — measured budget + LOD / lazy-load for 1000s of parts. | **WIRING-VOLTAGE-DROP-CALC** | **NEC 2023 voltage-drop calculator** — single-phase (V=2·I·L·R) and 3-phase (V=√3·I·L·R); NEC Ch9 Table 8 DC resistance (Cu + Al, AWG 14–4/0 + kcmil 250–750); temperature correction (α_Cu=0.00323, α_Al=0.00330/°C); NEC §215.2 3%/5% branch/system limit flags; honest-flag for AC reactance on ≥1/0 AWG; `wiring_voltage_drop` LLM tool. | Catches over-length runs at design time; NEC §215.2 compliance check built-in. | ✅ shipped — `kerf-wiring/voltage_drop.py`, `kerf-wiring/tools/wiring_voltage_drop.py`; 36 tests |
| **ELEC-VOLTAGE-DROP-CHECK** | **NEC 2023 Article 210.19(A) electronics voltage-drop check** — DC / single-phase / three-phase; NEC Ch9 Table 8 DC resistance at 75°C (Cu + Al, AWG 14–4/0 + 250 kcmil); IEEE 141 §3 formulas (DC: 2·I·R·L; 1φ: 2·I·R·L·PF; 3φ: √3·I·R·L·PF); NEC 210.19(A) Informational Note 4 advisory (≤3% feeder / ≤2% branch); `electronics_check_voltage_drop` LLM tool; `ConductorSpec` + `CircuitSpec` + `VoltageDropReport` dataclasses. Honest: 75°C copper baseline; no temperature correction; AC reactance ignored (≤5% error for AWG ≤ 2; 5–15% underestimate for ≥ 1/0 AWG at 60 Hz). | Catches over-length runs at design time; NEC 210.19(A) compliance check built-in for electronics/EDA context. | ✅ shipped — `kerf-electronics/voltage_drop.py`, `kerf-electronics/tools/voltage_drop.py`; 37 tests |
| **ELEC-CIRCUIT-PROTECTION-NEC-CHECK** | **NEC 2023 Article 240.4 + Table 310.16 + Article 215 circuit-protection check** — conductor ampacity from NEC Table 310.16 75°C column (Cu + Al, AWG 14–500 kcmil; THWN/THHN/XHHW/RHW); required OCPD = 1.25 × I_continuous + I_non_continuous (NEC 215.3 / 210.20(A)); NEC 240.4(B) OCPD ≤ ampacity; NEC 240.4(D) small-conductor cap (14 AWG Cu → 15 A, 12 → 20 A, 10 → 30 A); `electronics_check_circuit_protection` LLM tool; `ConductorSpec` + `LoadSpec` + `OcpdSpec` + `CircuitProtectionReport` dataclasses. Honest: 75°C THWN baseline; no ambient-temperature derating (NEC 310.15(B)(2)(a)); no conductor-bundling derating (NEC Table 310.15(B)(3)(a)); short-circuit withstand, arc-flash, and grounding out of scope. | Code-compliant OCPD sizing verification for branch circuits and feeders; catches undersized breakers and undersized conductors at design time. | ✅ shipped — `kerf-electronics/circuit_protection_check.py`, `kerf-electronics/tools/circuit_protection.py`; 43 tests |
| **ELEC-WIRE-AMPACITY-DERATE** | **NEC 2023 Article 310 wire ampacity derating** — ambient temperature correction (Table 310.15(B)(2)(a), 75°C insulation column: ≤30°C→1.00, 31–35→0.94, 36–40→0.88, 41–45→0.82, 46–50→0.75, 51–55→0.67, 56–60→0.58) + conductor bundling adjustment (Table 310.15(B)(3)(a): 1–3→1.00, 4–6→0.80, 7–9→0.70, 10–20→0.50, 21–30→0.45, 31–40→0.40, 41+→0.35); effective ampacity = base × C_ambient × C_bundle; `WireSpec` + `InstallationConditions` + `DeratedAmpacityReport` dataclasses; `electronics_compute_derated_ampacity` LLM tool. Honest: 75°C insulation column only (THWN/THHN/XHHW/RHW); rooftop adder (310.15(B)(3)(c)), underground/buried (Table 310.15(B)(7)), and Type NM cable derating NOT modelled; free-air (Table 310.17) not covered; ambient > 60°C out of range. | Catches installation-condition derating errors that circuit-protection check omits; critical for conduit fill + high-ambient industrial/outdoor runs. | ✅ shipped — `kerf-electronics/wire_ampacity_derate.py`, `kerf-electronics/tools/wire_ampacity_derate.py`; 56 tests |
| **ELEC-PCB-TRACE-CURRENT-CHECK** | **IPC-2221B simplified PCB trace maximum current** — IPC-2221B Eq. 6-4 empirical power-law: I [A] = k · ΔT^0.44 · A^0.725 where A [mil²] = trace_width_mils × (copper_oz × 1.37); k_external=0.048, k_internal=0.024; copper weights 0.5–3 oz/ft²; allowed temperature rise (default 10 °C); `PcbTraceSpec` + `PcbTraceCurrentReport` dataclasses; `electronics_compute_pcb_trace_current` LLM tool. Honest: IPC-2221B simplified formula only; IPC-2152 (2009) has more detailed thermal curves with copper-weight correction (cf_cw), board thermal-conductivity correction (cf_th), and plane-proximity correction (cf_pl) NOT modelled here — use `tracecurrent_ipc2152` for the full IPC-2152 model; no temperature-coefficient-of-resistivity correction; worst-case steady-state (no heat spreading from adjacent copper, vias, or pads). | Instant PCB trace ampacity check at design time without needing a full IPC-2152 calculator; catches undersized signal/power traces early. | ✅ shipped — `kerf-electronics/pcb_trace_current.py`, `kerf-electronics/tools/pcb_trace_current.py`; 27 tests |

## Planned next

### Depth gaps (concrete, near-term)

| # | Gap | vs | Status |
|---|---|---|---|
| G-2 | **ELEC-DECOUPLING-CAP-SIZE: decoupling capacitor sizing for digital ICs** — Z_target = ΔV/I_transient (Howard Johnson §8.3); C_bulk = I·t_rise/ΔV (Ott §13.3.3 charge balance); bypass 100 nF/IC (≤50 MHz) or 10 nF/IC (>50 MHz); max ESL per cap = Z_target/(2π·f_bw); `PowerRailSpec` + `DecouplingRecommendation` dataclasses; `electronics_recommend_decoupling_caps` LLM tool. Honest: target-impedance heuristic only; PDN simulation (SPICE/pdn_decap_wizard) required for anti-resonance validation. | Altium PDN Analyzer | ✅ shipped — `kerf-electronics/decoupling_cap_size.py`; 32 tests |
| G-2b | **ELEC-DIFFPAIR-SKEW: intra-pair length-matching skew check** — v = c/√εr (c=0.3 mm/ps); Δt = |ΔL|/v; protocol budgets: HDMI 2.1=15 ps, USB 3.0=20 ps, PCIe 4.0=2 ps, DDR5=5 ps, SATA III=15 ps (Johnson §12.4 + IPC-2141A §6); `DiffPairSpec` + `DiffPairSkewReport` dataclasses; `electronics_check_diffpair_skew` LLM tool; custom budget override. Honest: assumes uniform effective εr (±5–15% actual variation per IPC-2141A §6.2); meander-delay skew NOT modelled (Johnson §12.4); via/connector transitions and inter-pair skew out of scope. | KiCad DRC / Altium SI | ✅ shipped — `kerf-electronics/diffpair_skew_check.py`; 30 tests |
| G-2c | **ELEC-CRYSTAL-OSC-LOAD-CAP: Pierce crystal oscillator external load capacitor calculator** — CL = (C1·C2)/(C1+C2) + C_stray (NXP AN-2867 §3 + AVR ATmega §28.5); symmetric design C1=C2=2·(CL−C_stray); asymmetric verification mode back-computes effective CL; qualitative gain-margin check using pessimistic gm=4 mA/V heuristic (NXP AN-2867 §4.2 requires ≥5× ESR); `CrystalSpec` (frequency_MHz, load_capacitance_CL_pF, esr_max_ohms, drive_level_uW) + `PCBLayoutSpec` (pcb_stray_capacitance_pF=2.0, mcu_pad_capacitance_pF=1.0) + `CrystalLoadCapReport` dataclasses; `electronics_compute_crystal_load_caps` LLM tool. Honest: (1) drive-level limiting NOT modelled — P_d = ½·ESR·(ω·C_eff·V_osc)² must be verified against crystal rating; (2) PI-network compensation for >20 MHz crystals NOT applied (NXP AN-2867 §3.3); (3) C_stray is a first-order estimate, measure on target board. | KiCad / Altium oscillator wizard | ✅ shipped — `kerf-electronics/crystal_load_cap.py`; 25 tests |

| G-15 | **BIM site / earthwork (toposolids)** | Revit / Civil 3D | ✅ shipped — toposolid B-rep grading + IFC site export — `kerf-bim/tools/site_geometry.py`, `kerf-bim/site_ifc.py` |
| G-16 | **BIM material catalogue with render appearance** | Revit / Enscape | ✅ shipped — 40+ materials with PBR properties (`base_color`, `metallic`, `roughness`, `ior`, `transmission`) wired to Cycles translator — `kerf-bim/material_catalogue.py` |

### Long-tail verticals

Everything committed, lowest priority. Ordered roughly by near-term readiness.

**Mechanical / product:** cams generators · woodworking / furniture / joinery + cutlist · power one-line / switchgear · lighting / photometric · interior / space-planning / FF&E *(IFC 4 export (ISO 16739-1:2018) ✅ — subset export, NOT buildingSMART certified; `kerf-interior/ifc_export.py`)* · kitchen / bath / cabinetry / millwork · landscape · scaffolding / formwork.

| Woodworking | Capability | Status |
|---|---|---|
| Joinery geometry validator (Hammer-Krenov) | Validate dovetail (7°–14° pin angle, ≥1/3 board pin width, ≥2 pins), mortise-and-tenon (1/3-rule, cheek check, tenon length), box joint (≥3 fingers, equal widths, depth==thickness), finger joint (angle 15±3°); strength estimate via FPL Wood Handbook shear values × joint efficiency for oak/pine/cherry/maple/walnut in kN; `woodworking_validate_joinery` + `woodworking_joinery_strength` LLM tools | ✅ shipped — `kerf-woodworking/joinery_validate.py` |
**Mechanical / product:** cams generators · woodworking / furniture / joinery + cutlist · power one-line / switchgear · lighting / photometric · interior / space-planning / FF&E · kitchen / bath / cabinetry / millwork · landscape (plant catalog with USDA + Dirr references, 101 species ✅) · scaffolding / formwork.

**Vehicles:** composites ply/layup authoring (draping / fiber-steering / Fibersim class) · hull fairing (NURBS-reachable) · 3D harness routing.

**Civil / infrastructure (distinct engines):** plan-and-profile sheet engine · IFC-4.3-infra I/O · bridge/tunnel · mining · marine/dredging · rail signaling. *(CRS engine, horizontal/vertical alignment, corridor, earthworks, geotechnical, LandXML 1.2 I/O, pressurized water-distribution networks (Todini GGA + Hazen-Williams/Darcy-Weisbach), gravity sewer (Manning), storm rational method + HDS-5 culverts already shipped; TINView / PipeNetworkView / GradingPlanView / LandscapeView UIs ✅ 2026-05-29.)*

**Body-worn / medical / craft:** watchmaking / horology · eyewear / frames · footwear / last design · dental CAD (crowns/aligners) · orthopedic / prosthetics · hearing aids.

**Soft goods (distinct 2D/developable engine):** apparel / pattern-making + drape · technical textiles / sails / membrane / tensile · upholstery / leather. *(ARAP/LSCM pattern flattening for non-developable surfaces (Bo-Wang 2007 / Lévy 2002) ✅ — `kerf-apparel/pattern_flatten.py`, `apparel_flatten_pattern` LLM tool wired.)*
**Soft goods (distinct 2D/developable engine):** apparel / pattern-making + drape · technical textiles / sails / membrane / tensile · upholstery / leather. *(ASTM D5219 + ISO 8559 grading rules ✅ — `GradingRule`, `build_grading_table`, `apply_grading`, `grade_check_iso_8559` shipped; `apparel_apply_grading` + `apparel_grade_check` LLM tools registered — `packages/kerf-apparel/src/kerf_apparel/grading.py`.)*

**Scientific / niche:** microfluidics / MEMS · signage / large-format.

**Silicon next:** verification depth + post-silicon (cocotb testbench harness, power analysis, STA, clock-tree synthesis, formal equivalence, Tiny Tapeout / Efabless harnesses). T-249..T-258.

**Firmware next:** RTOS primitives, OTA, RTOS-aware debugger, power profiling, pin-map cross-check vs PCB, USB-class drivers. T-259..T-265. **T-274 ✅** — Build / Flash / Monitor UI wired: `FirmwareProjectPanel`, `BuildOutput`, `SerialMonitor` in `src/components/firmware/`; `firmware_project` kind renders in Editor; PlatformIO + Arduino IDE compare rows added.

**Aerospace next:** XFOIL-class viscous solver, aircraft conceptual sizing (Raymer/Roskam), stability derivatives, aero-acoustics (FW-H), heat-shield/ablation, aerospace fasteners. T-266..T-272.

**Platform (demand-gated post-launch):** fully-local / offline / no-account desktop app — committed but not a launch pillar. Portability + two-way sync + easy self-host is the launch answer.

### Strategic AI-native capabilities

These are roadmap-level moats that span every sector simultaneously and compound leverage instead of adding it linearly.

| **PLM depth** — configurator, 150% / effectivity BOM, where-used, ECR/ECO, digital thread, MBSE/SysML traceability. File revisions + cloud git + configurations + BOM rollup shipped. **BOM Cost Roll-up (ISO 10303-44 + APICS "rolled-up cost") ✅** — `packages/kerf-plm/src/kerf_plm/bom_cost_rollup.py`; LLM tool: `plm_rollup_bom_cost`. Recursive depth-first post-order rollup: `rolled_cost(node) = internal_cost + Σ(qty_i × rolled_cost(child_i))`; `BomNode` dataclass (part_number, name, unit_cost, currency, children, internal_cost); `RollupReport` (total_cost, currency, num_unique_parts, depth, cost_breakdown_by_node, honest_caveat); FX conversion via caller-supplied `fx_rates` dict (default 2025 baseline: USD/EUR/GBP/ZAR/JPY/CAD/AUD/CHF/CNY/INR); cycle detection (ValueError with full path); fractional quantities; multi-currency trees. Honest-flagged: static unit costs only — no scrap, overhead absorption, yield-based costing, learning-curve amortisation, or activity-based costing. References: ISO 10303-44:2021 §5.3; APICS Dictionary 16th ed.; Horngren et al. §7. 20 hermetic tests green. | ✅ shipped |
| **PLM depth** — configurator, 150% / effectivity BOM, where-used, ECR/ECO, digital thread, MBSE/SysML traceability. File revisions + cloud git + configurations + BOM rollup shipped. **Component Where-Used (ISO 10303-44 + APICS "where-used") ✅** — `packages/kerf-plm/src/kerf_plm/component_whereused.py`; LLM tool: `plm_component_whereused`. Given a flat list of `BomRelationship(parent_pn, child_pn, qty)` records, performs BFS upward from the queried component to root assemblies; returns `WhereUsedReport` (component_pn, num_unique_parents, num_total_usages, max_depth, entries, honest_caveat) and per-entry `WhereUsedEntry` (parent_pn, parent_name, qty, level); qty aggregation: multiple rows for the same (parent, child) pair are summed; BFS first-visit ensures shallowest level wins for diamond BOMs; cycle detection raises ValueError with full cycle path. Honest-flagged: in-memory traversal only — no DB pagination, live PDM sync, effectivity filtering, or path-multiplied extended-qty. References: ISO 10303-44:2021 §5.3 (next_assembly_usage_occurrence); APICS Dictionary 16th ed. "where-used"; PROSTEP-iViP SIG §5.2. 17 hermetic tests green. | ✅ shipped |
| **PLM depth** — **ECN Cascading Impact Analysis (ISO 10007 §6 + APICS "ECN") ✅** — `packages/kerf-plm/src/kerf_plm/ecn_impact_analysis.py`; LLM tool: `plm_analyze_ecn_impact`. Given an `EcnInput` (ecn_id, affected_components, change_description, urgency) + flat BOM relationships, performs BFS upward from every ECN-affected component to find all transitively affected parent assemblies (deduplicated across components); counts distinct drawings and open work orders linked to affected parents; heuristic cost estimate: `parents×$50 + drawings×cost_per_rev + work_orders×$200` (default $150/drawing); ISO 10007 §6.3.2 implementation class assignment: `Class_I_immediate` (emergency urgency OR ≥ 20 parents), `Class_II_rev` (normal, 1–19 parents), `Class_III_drawing_only` (deferred or zero parents). Honest-flagged: cost formula is heuristic — real-world ECN costs vary widely by industry; aerospace/defence drawing revisions can exceed $10 000; consumer electronics may be <$50; use for initial prioritisation only. Class assignment is heuristic; real ECN classification requires change-board review per ISO 10007 §6.5. 23 hermetic tests green. | ✅ shipped |
| **PLM depth** — **ECN Change-Log Export (ISO 10007 §6 + PMI PMBOK §4.6) ✅** — `packages/kerf-plm/src/kerf_plm/change_log_export.py`; LLM tool: `plm_export_change_log`. `EcnLogEntry` dataclass (ecn_id, summary, approval_date ISO 8601, status draft/approved/in_progress/closed/cancelled, affected_components, urgency emergency/normal/deferred, requester, approver); `ChangeLogExportResult` (csv_content RFC 4180, html_content table with thead/tbody, num_entries, date_range_start, date_range_end, summary_stats {total, by_status, by_urgency}, honest_caveat); `export_change_log(entries, start_date, end_date, sort_by)` — optional date-range filter (ISO 8601 bounds, entries with empty approval_date excluded when bounds set); sort by approval_date (default ascending), urgency (emergency first), status, or ecn_id; CSV uses csv.QUOTE_ALL (RFC 4180-compliant; commas in summary safely quoted); HTML table with status/urgency CSS colour cues. Honest-flagged: in-memory export only — no DB pagination for large change-log sets; all entries must fit in RAM; sorting is lexicographic ISO 8601; UTC timezone normalisation is caller's responsibility. References: ISO 10007:2003 §6; PMI PMBOK 7th ed. §4.6. 24 hermetic tests green. | ✅ shipped |
| **PLM depth** — **BOM Maturity Check (NASA TRL 1–9 + ISO/IEC 15288:2023 §6.3) ✅** — `packages/kerf-plm/src/kerf_plm/maturity_check.py`; LLM tool: `plm_assess_bom_maturity`. `ComponentMaturity` dataclass (part_number, trl_level 1–9, manufacturer_qualified, has_drawings, has_supplier, has_test_data); `MaturityReport` (parent_pn, weighted_avg_trl, blocker_count, risk_level, recommendation, honest_caveat); `assess_bom_maturity(parent_pn, children, qty_per_child)` — quantity-weighted average TRL roll-up; blocker_count = count(TRL < 5); risk bands: TRL ≥ 7 → low, 5–6 → medium, 3–4 → high, < 3 or any TRL ≤ 2 → critical. Honest-flagged: TRL weighted average is a simplified proxy — real maturity assessments also include test heritage, supplier capability maturity (AS9100 / CMMI), demonstrated performance in operational environment, FMEA closure, and PPAP evidence packages; a single low-TRL component can block a programme regardless of the mean score; risk bands are kerf heuristics and do not replace a formal SRR/PDR/CDR gate review per ISO/IEC 15288:2023 §6.3. References: NASA SP-2016-6105 Rev 2; ISO/IEC 15288:2023 §6.3; INCOSE SE Handbook v4 §4.1. 24 hermetic tests green. | ✅ shipped |
| **PLM depth** — **Part Obsolescence Check (IEC 62402 + DMSMS handbook) ✅** — `packages/kerf-plm/src/kerf_plm/part_obsolescence_check.py`; LLM tool: `plm_check_part_obsolescence`. `PartLifecycleStatus` string-constant class (active, preferred, NRND, LTB, EOL, obsolete); `PartLifecycleEntry` dataclass (part_number, manufacturer, status, last_buy_date, alternative_pn); `ObsolescenceReport` (total_parts, num_active, num_at_risk, num_obsolete, risk_score 0–100, critical_part_alerts, affected_assemblies, honest_caveat); `check_part_obsolescence(parts, bom_relationships)` — risk score formula per IEC 62402 §5.3 heuristic: `(NRND×1 + LTB×3 + EOL×5 + obsolete×10) / total_parts × 10`; critical_part_alerts populated for EOL and obsolete parts with alternative_pn pass-through; affected_assemblies derived from flat bom_relationships (deduplicated). Honest-flagged: lifecycle data is caller-supplied — no live IHS Markit / Octopart / Silicon Expert API integration included; callers must refresh lifecycle entries from their preferred data source (distributor feeds, ERP lifecycle fields, quarterly DMSMS scans); risk weights are kerf heuristics — calibrate to your supply-chain lead time and strategic-stock policy per DMSMS handbook §2.3; affected_assemblies is flat depth-1 only. References: IEC 62402:2019; US DoD DMSMS Handbook (2018) §2.3 + §4.1; JEDEC JEP106. 26 hermetic tests green. | ✅ shipped |
| **PLM depth** — **Variant Configuration (PLM-VARIANT-CONFIG) ✅** — `packages/kerf-plm/src/kerf_plm/variant_config.py`; LLM tool: `plm_resolve_variant_bom`. `VariantRule` dataclass (part_number, variant_attribute_key e.g. "color"/"region"/"market_segment", variant_attribute_value, condition "include"\|"exclude"); `VariantSelection` dataclass (variant_id, attributes dict[str,str]); `VariantResolvedBomEntry` dataclass (part_number, qty, included, reason); `VariantConfigReport` (variant_id, num_total_parts, num_included_parts, num_excluded_parts, resolved_bom, honest_caveat); `resolve_variant_bom(base_bom, variant_rules, variant)` — for each part: collect rules matching part_number + attribute key=value (exact-match, implicit AND for multi-attribute queries); first-match-per-part semantics (declaration order); parts with no matching rule ALWAYS INCLUDED (open-world default, ISO 10303-44 §6.2); report accessors: `included_parts()` → [(pn, qty)], `excluded_parts()` → [pn]. Honest-flagged: simple rule-based variant selection — NO formal feature-model solver, NO constraint propagation, NO cardinality constraints, NO mutual-exclusion groups; complex AND/OR/NOT variant expressions not supported in v1; use FeatureIDE/SPLOT for full ISO 10303-44 §6 constraint solving. References: PTC Windchill Variant Management; ISO 10303-44:2000 §6; Saaksvuori & Immonen "Product Lifecycle Management" §4.3. 18 hermetic tests green. | ✅ shipped |
| **PLM depth** — **BOM Revision Compare Diff (PLM-BOM-COMPARE-DIFF) ✅** — `packages/kerf-plm/src/kerf_plm/bom_compare_diff.py`; LLM tool: `plm_compare_boms`. `BomLineItem` dataclass (part_number, qty, description); `BomDiffEntry` (part_number, change_type added\|removed\|qty_increased\|qty_decreased\|unchanged, old_qty, new_qty, qty_delta); `BomDiffReport` (total_parts_old, total_parts_new, num_added, num_removed, num_qty_changed, num_unchanged, diff_entries sorted by part_number, honest_caveat); `compare_boms(old_bom, new_bom)` — keys on part_number (case-sensitive); duplicate part_numbers collapsed (last-write-wins); qty_delta signed: +new_qty for added, -old_qty for removed, new-old for changes. Honest-flagged: flat single-level BOM diff only — no hierarchy traversal, no where-used cascade, no effectivity/variant expansion, no description-change detection, no PN alias normalisation. - **NURBS-SURFACE-SHEAR-OFFSET** ✅ — `apply_shear_offset(surface, shear: ShearMatrix) → SurfaceShearOffsetResult`; apply a global linear shear-transform (I+S) to all control points of a NurbsSurface: P'_x = x + s_xy·y + s_xz·z, P'_y = y + s_yx·x + s_yz·z, P'_z = z + s_zx·x + s_zy·y (Mortenson §4.8; Piegl & Tiller §6.1 Theorem 6.1). `ShearMatrix` dataclass: six off-diagonal shear coefficients (s_xy, s_xz, s_yx, s_yz, s_zx, s_zy; all default 0.0). `SurfaceShearOffsetResult`: sheared_surface, max_displacement_mm, mean_displacement_mm, honest_caveat. Knots and weights preserved exactly. LLM tool `nurbs_apply_surface_shear_offset` registered (gated import); re-exported from `geom/__init__.py`; 20 hermetic tests (identity unchanged, zero displacement, single-axis oracles for all 6 coefficients, combined superposition, knot/weight preservation, rational weight copy, max/mean displacement formulas, max≥mean invariant, ValueError for non-3D CPs, ShearMatrix defaults, input not mutated, honest caveat content). HONEST: global linear shear only — non-uniform warp (thermal distortion, springback, gravity sag) requires per-point deformation field, not a single ShearMatrix; displacement stats are control-point displacements, not evaluated-surface deviations — `kerf-cad-core/geom/surface_shear_offset.py`.
- **NURBS-CURVE-FOOTPRINT-ON-PLANE** ✅ — `project_curve_to_plane(curve, plane_point, plane_normal) → FootprintResult`; orthographic projection of a 3-D NurbsCurve onto an arbitrary plane, producing a planar 2-D NurbsCurve in plane-local UV coordinates. `FootprintResult` dataclass: `footprint_curve_2d`, `projection_axis`, `max_orig_depth`, `honest_caveat`. Each control point projected via P' = P − ((P−O)·n̂) n̂; degree, knot vector and weights preserved exactly (Piegl & Tiller §6.1 Theorem 6.1). Degenerate flag when curve is perpendicular to the plane (footprint collapses to a point). `lift_footprint_to_3d` inverse helper. LLM tool `nurbs_curve_project_to_plane` registered (gated import). Re-exported from `geom/__init__.py`. 17 hermetic analytic-oracle tests (helix→XY circle radius exact, already-planar identity, vertical-line degenerate, skewed-normal unit-axis, knot/weight/degree preservation, non-rational weights=None, max_orig_depth, projection-formula depth, 45°-tilt analytic, make_circle_nurbs round-trip, lift round-trip, ValueError zero-normal, multi-turn helix, YZ-plane analytic). HONEST: orthographic (linear) projection only — no perspective; for rational NURBS the footprint is a correct rational NURBS but the Euclidean evaluated curve may differ from a naive point-by-point projection. Refs: Piegl & Tiller §6.1; Mortenson §4.4 — `kerf-cad-core/geom/curve_footprint_on_plane.py`.
- **NURBS-CURVE-CURVATURE-OSCULATING-CIRCLE** ✅ — osculating circle at any parameter t: `osculating_circle(curve, t) → OsculatingCircle` (center, radius, tangent, curvature, normal_plane_normal, is_degenerate) + `osculating_circles_along(curve, samples)`; κ = |C′×C″|/|C′|³ (do Carmo §1.5); degenerate sentinel (κ=0 → radius=None, is_degenerate=True); LLM tool `nurbs_osculating_circle` registered; re-exported from `geom/__init__.py`; 18 hermetic tests — circle oracle (κ=1/R ±1e-6, center=origin), line oracle (κ=0, degenerate), helix κ=0.5/radius=2.0, parabola vertex κ=2/radius=0.5, sample-grid — `geom/osculating_circle.py`.
- **NURBS-NORMAL-CURVATURE-AT-POINT** ✅ — normal curvature κ_n = II(t,t)/I(t,t) via Meusnier's theorem (do Carmo §3.2 / Mortenson §10.4); `normal_curvature_at(srf, u, v, direction_uv) → NormalCurvatureReport` (κ_n, κ_1, κ_2, K, H, principal_dirs, is_umbilic, is_degenerate); principal curvatures from characteristic equation of shape operator; Euler's formula κ_n(θ)=κ_1cos²(θ-φ)+κ_2sin²(θ-φ) verified; umbilic honest-flag (κ_1=κ_2 → principal_dirs=None); LLM tool `nurbs_normal_curvature_at_point` registered; re-exported from `geom/__init__.py`; 32 hermetic analytic-oracle tests — sphere K=1/|κ_n|=1 in 12 dirs, cylinder κ_along=0/|κ_across|=1/R/K=0, saddle K<0/mixed-sign principals, Euler formula bounded in all dirs — `geom/normal_curvature.py`.
- **NURBS-FAIR-COMPOSITE-CURVE** ✅ — `composite_fair.py`: `fair_composite(curves, max_iter=50, lambda_smoothness=1.0)` — global curvature-variance fairing for poly-NURBS chains; minimises Σ‖D²P‖² (discrete bending energy, Greiner-Hormann 1996 §3.2) over all segments with per-iteration G1 seam re-imposition (Klass 1980 §3 bisector) and hard-pinned global endpoints (≤1e-6); honest `converged=False` flag for anti-parallel seams or stalled descent; returns `CompositeFairResult` (faired_curves, curvature_variance_before/after, iterations, converged, endpoint_error); `nurbs_fair_composite` LLM tool; 10 hermetic tests — 3-segment kink ≥50% variance reduction, smooth arc not degraded, endpoints within 1e-6.

NURBS↔Mesh reconciliation with fidelity tracking (Lévy 2009) ✅ — `geom/mesh_reconciliation.py`; two-sided Hausdorff deviation metric, extras detection, round-trip pipeline, feature-line-guided fit; LLM tools `brep_reconcile_nurbs_mesh` + `brep_round_trip_with_fidelity`.
- **GK-P SubD / mesh** — multires displacement; SDF CSG + marching-cubes; sculpt brush engine; LSCM UV unwrap (module exists, wiring incomplete); SubD cage derivation from dense mesh (Lee-Moreton-Hoppe 2000) ✅.
- **GK-P SubD / mesh** — multires displacement; SDF CSG + marching-cubes; sculpt brush engine; LSCM UV unwrap (module exists, wiring incomplete). **SubD edge flow optimization (Bommes 2009) ✅** — `geom/subd_edge_flow.py`; `subd_optimize_edge_flow` LLM tool registered.
- **GK-P SubD / mesh** — multires displacement; SDF CSG + marching-cubes; sculpt brush engine; LSCM UV unwrap (module exists, wiring incomplete); SubD cage optimization for limit constraints ✅.
- **GK-P SubD / mesh** — multires displacement; SDF CSG + marching-cubes; sculpt brush engine; LSCM UV unwrap (module exists, wiring incomplete). SubD normal-color map + GLB vertex-color export ✅
- **GK-P SubD / mesh** — multires displacement; SDF CSG + marching-cubes; sculpt brush engine; LSCM UV unwrap (module exists, wiring incomplete). OpenSubdiv-compatible SubD export (Pixar OSD 3.5) ✅ — `subd_opensubdiv_export.py`; OBJ/JSON/binary formats + compatibility checker + subdivision pyramid. SubD USD export (USDA ASCII, catmullClark, creases) ✅ — `subd_export_usd.py`; `export_subd_to_usda` + `parse_usda_subd` round-trip; LLM tool `subd_export_to_usd`; targets HdStorm/Houdini/Maya USD workflows; USDC binary out of scope. **SUBD-LIMIT-MESH-EXPORT-OBJ** ✅ — `subd_export_obj.py`; `export_limit_to_obj(cage, levels=2, include_normals=True) -> str` + `parse_obj` round-trip; LLM tool `subd_export_limit_to_obj`; cube cage 2 levels → 96 quads; face count scales 4× per level; bounding-box convergence verified. Geometry only — no MTL; vertex normals via area-weighted cross-product (not Stam exact eigenbasis); re-exported from `geom/__init__.py`.
- **GK-P SubD / mesh** — multires displacement; SDF CSG + marching-cubes; sculpt brush engine; LSCM UV unwrap (module exists, wiring incomplete). **SUBD-EXPORT-PLY** ✅ — `subd_export_ply.py`; `export_limit_to_ply(cage, levels=2, format="ascii") -> bytes` + `parse_ply` round-trip; LLM tool `subd_export_limit_to_ply`; ASCII and binary_little_endian; valid PLY header (ply, format, element vertex N, property float x/y/z, element face F, property list uchar int vertex_indices, end_header); cube cage 2 levels → 96 faces; binary body compact vs ASCII; sphere cage bounding-box convergence. Honest (v1): geometry only — no colour, normals, texture coords; no big-endian; pure-Python struct module. 36 tests. Ref: Turk (1994) Stanford PLY spec. **SUBD-EXPORT-GLTF** ✅ — `subd_export_gltf.py`; `export_limit_to_gltf(cage, levels=2, format="gltf") -> bytes` + `parse_gltf` round-trip; both `.gltf` (JSON + base64 buffer) and `.glb` (binary GLB container) formats; valid `asset.version="2.0"`; POSITION (VEC3 FLOAT) + SCALAR UNSIGNED_INT indices; quads fan-triangulated; GLB magic b"glTF" + version 2; cube cage 2 levels → 192 triangles; vertex/face counts round-trip; sphere cage bounding-box convergence. Honest (v1): geometry only — no materials, normals attribute, textures, animations, skinning; no Draco compression; pure-Python (json + struct). 39 tests. LLM tool `subd_export_limit_to_gltf`. Ref: Khronos glTF 2.0 https://www.khronos.org/gltf/ **SUBD-EXPORT-STEP** ✅ — `subd_export_step.py`; `export_limit_to_step(cage, levels=2) -> str` + `parse_step_subd` round-trip; valid ISO 10303-21 STEP AP242 ASCII file; FILE_DESCRIPTION + FILE_NAME + FILE_SCHEMA + DATA section; CARTESIAN_POINT / VERTEX_POINT / EDGE_CURVE / EDGE_LOOP / FACE_OUTER_BOUND / ADVANCED_FACE on PLANE surfaces / OPEN_SHELL / SHELL_BASED_SURFACE_MODEL / SHAPE_REPRESENTATION; minimal SI unit context (millimetres); cube cage 2 levels → 96 ADVANCED_FACEs; face count scales 4× per level; sphere cage bounding-box convergence; structural validity verified (header + DATA + ENDSEC). Honest: faceted B-rep — each subdivided polygon is a flat PLANE face (STEP has no native SubD primitive); not smooth NURBS. Pure-Python. 38 tests. LLM tool `subd_export_limit_to_step`. Ref: ISO 10303-242:2020, ISO 10303-42:2022, ISO 10303-21:2016.
- **GK-P architectural geometry** — B-rep→2D tessellate; roof/curtain-wall/corridor generators; wall compound-layer offset; hatch/section-fill.
- **GK-P sketcher** — collinear constraint; ellipse solver entity; G2 continuity. **Parametric sketch constraint solver (Sutherland 1963 / Hoffmann 2001) ✅** — Newton-Raphson DOF solver with Jacobian numerical differentiation, 10 constraint kinds (coincident/horizontal/vertical/parallel/perpendicular/tangent/distance/angle/equal/on_curve), `check_consistency` (over/under detection via rank), `drag_entity` interactive re-solve, 2 LLM tools (`nurbs_sketch_solver`, `nurbs_sketch_drag`) — `geom/sketch_solver.py`.
