(Acoustics FEM, EM, harmonic, buckling, PSD, multi-axial fatigue, explicit dynamics are now all shipped.)
- **T-100 FEM depth** ✅ EPIC CLOSED — all sub-tasks shipped: explicit dynamics, full nonlinear static (geometric + material + contact + arc-length), k-ε turbulence CFD, coupled-field probabilistic FEA (LHS + Karhunen-Loève), plus acoustics FEM, EM, harmonic, buckling, PSD, multi-axial fatigue.
- **Composite curve G2 audit + upgrade** ✅ — `composite_g2.py`: `audit_composite_g2` (per-joint G0/G1/G2 residuals), `upgrade_to_g2` (cubic Hermite / quintic Bezier blend insertion), `composite_curvature_profile` (κ(s) statistics + jump detection); LLM tools `nurbs_composite_g2_audit` + `nurbs_composite_g2_upgrade` registered; 4 validation test classes (27 tests green).
- **GK-P rational conic detection** ✅ — `detect_conic` / `extract_canonical_circle` / `simplify_curve`; Lee 1987 algebraic LS fit + Piegl-Tiller §7.2 classification; returns `ConicInfo` (center, axes, radii, eccentricity, focus, plane_normal) for circle / ellipse / parabola / hyperbola; 2 LLM tools (`nurbs_detect_conic`, `nurbs_simplify_conic`); 24 hermetic analytic-oracle tests — `geom/conic_detect.py`.
- **GK-P NURBS↔mesh max deviation** — NURBS surface ↔ triangle mesh Hausdorff distance + per-region max + RMS (Aspert-Santa-Cruz-Ebrahimi 2002 / Cignoni-Rocchini-Scopigno 1998); critical for class-A reverse-engineering acceptance (point cloud → NURBS fit). LLM tool: `nurbs_max_deviation_to_mesh`. ✅
- **GK-P auto-lightweight** — Auto-lightweight body (Lyche-Mørken knot removal + rational simplification) ✅ — `geom/auto_lightweight.py`; `brep_auto_lightweight` LLM tool; 4 hermetic oracle tests.
- **NURBS-CURVE-CIRCLE-FIT** ✅ — fit a circle to a 2D NurbsCurve by least-squares (Kasa 1976 + Taubin 1991); reports center, radius, RMS and max residual; `nurbs_fit_circle_to_curve` LLM tool wired. Caveats: 2D only — for 3D space curves project onto a plane first; short arcs (< 30°) prefer Taubin. Ref: Taubin (1991) IEEE TPAMI 13(11):1115–1138; Kasa (1976) IEEE TIM 25(1):8–14.
- **NURBS-CURVE-LINE-FIT** ✅ — fit a straight line to a 2D NurbsCurve via total-least-squares (TLS) / SVD; `LineFitResult(origin_xy, direction_xy, rms_residual_mm, max_residual_mm, is_planar_line, honest_caveat)`; `fit_line_to_curve` + `nurbs_fit_line_to_curve` LLM tool wired; 35 hermetic tests. Algorithm: centroid subtraction + thin SVD; principal right-singular vector = least-squares line direction; perpendicular residuals computed orthogonally. Use cases: linear-segment detection in imported STEP/IGES profiles, snap-to-line in 2D sketcher, near-straight edge classification. HONEST: 2D only — for 3D space curves project onto a plane first; for 3D principal-axis fit use 3D SVD separately; direction is undirected (unit vector, sign-canonicalised); sampling is parameter-uniform, not arc-length-uniform. Refs: Press §15.7 (TLS); Lawson-Hanson §6 (SVD geometric fitting). `geom/curve_line_fit.py`; re-exported from `geom/__init__.py`.
- **NURBS-CURVE-CONIC-DETECT** ✅ — `detect_conic_type(curve_or_points, num_samples=100, residual_threshold_mm=0.01)` returns `ConicDetectResult(conic_type, conic_coefficients, eccentricity, rms_residual_mm, honest_caveat)`; classifies a 2-D NurbsCurve or raw point set as one of: `circle` | `ellipse` | `parabola` | `hyperbola` | `line` | `free_form`. Algorithm: (1) sample `num_samples` 2-D points; (2) line gate — if TLS perpendicular-distance RMS < `residual_threshold_mm` → `"line"`; (3) fit the general conic Ax²+Bxy+Cy²+Dx+Ey+F=0 via SVD null-space (smallest right-singular vector), normalised so Frobenius norm of the quadratic block [[A, B/2],[B/2, C]] = 1; (4) if RMS pseudo-geometric residual > `residual_threshold_mm` → `"free_form"`; (5) classify by discriminant Δ = B²−4AC: Δ < −ε → ellipse-family (circle if additionally |B| < ε_c and |A−C| < ε_c·max(|A|,|C|)), |Δ| ≤ ε → parabola, Δ > ε → hyperbola. Eccentricity: 0 for circle, sqrt(1−b²/a²) for ellipse, 1 for parabola, sqrt(1+b²/a²) for hyperbola (axes extracted from 3×3 homogeneous conic matrix eigendecomposition). LLM tool `nurbs_detect_conic_type` registered (gated import). Re-exported from `geom/__init__.py`. 32 hermetic tests (circle r=1, circle r=5, ellipse a=3/b=1 e≈0.9428, parabola y=x²/2, horizontal line, tilted line, sinusoid free_form, random free_form, rectangular hyperbola xy=1, coefficient round-trip, raw-point array, threshold gate, degenerate < 5 points). **HONEST CAVEATS**: (1) Algebraic least-squares fit is biased by gradient magnitude — for production-quality circle detection use Pratt (1987) or Taubin (1991) in `curve_circle_fit.py`. (2) Parabola detection via discriminant thresholding is fragile near the parabolic boundary for noisy data — the Δ=0 locus is a measure-zero set. (3) The `rms_residual_mm` is a *pseudo-geometric* residual (algebraic value / gradient magnitude), not the true Euclidean distance to the conic. (4) Line detection uses TLS perpendicular RMS exclusively (degenerate conic Bxy+Dx+Ey+F=0 has nonzero quadratic-block norm, so a separate geometric test is needed). Refs: Pratt, V. (1987) "Direct least-squares fitting of algebraic surfaces." SIGGRAPH §3; Fitzgibbon, A., Pilu, M., & Fisher, R.B. (1999) "Direct least-square fitting of ellipses." IEEE TPAMI 21(5):476–480. `geom/curve_conic_detect.py`; re-exported from `geom/__init__.py`.
- **BREP-EDGE-FACE-NORMAL-FLIP** ✅ — detect and fix B-rep faces whose outward normals are inconsistently oriented (some inverted) via iterative neighbour-consensus BFS voting. `FaceNormalFlipResult` dataclass: `face_normals_after`, `num_faces_flipped`, `flipped_face_indices`, `consensus_score`, `honest_caveat`. `detect_and_flip_face_normals(faces_with_normals, max_iter=10, threshold=0.15)`: for each BFS edge (A→B), if dot(n_A, n_B) < -threshold (anti-parallel, indicating face B is inverted relative to the expected co-oriented outward direction of a convex surface) → flip face B. Iterates until convergence. LLM tool `brep_detect_and_flip_face_normals` registered in `plugin.py`. Re-exported from `geom/__init__.py`. 16 hermetic tests. **Honest caveats**: (1) PERPENDICULAR-FACE LIMITATION — adjacent faces with orthogonal normals (|dot|≤threshold, e.g. unit cube) produce no flip signal; a cube cannot be corrected from normals alone. (2) Algorithm assumes CONVEX surface convention (adjacent outward normals co-oriented, dot>0); NOT valid for concave surfaces or open flat meshes where inversion produces co-oriented pairs. (3) Isolated faces (no neighbour_face_indices) are returned unchanged. (4) Absolute orientation is seeded from the first face per connected component — all-inward input is internally consistent but absolutely wrong. (5) Not a geometric B-rep heal: does not recompute normals from surface derivatives; for production use OCCT BRepLib::OrientClosedSolid. Refs: Mantyla §6.4; Hoffmann §3; Weiler 1985 §3. `geom/face_normal_flip.py`; re-exported from `geom/__init__.py`.
- **T-100 FEM depth** — explicit dynamics (module exists, not yet imported/registered); full nonlinear static (only 1-D bar/truss shipped); k-ε turbulence CFD; coupled FEA-based variation analysis. (Acoustics FEM, EM, harmonic, buckling, PSD, multi-axial fatigue are now shipped.)

---

## Deliberately not building

This list is only AI-redundant *authoring/UX interaction paradigms* — not skipped domains or correctness features.

| Not building | Why |
|---|---|
| Visual node programming (Grasshopper / Dynamo / Sverchok) | The LLM writing a parametric script *is* the graph. `.script.py` + SDKs + JSCAD + `.graph` cover the value. |
| Ribbon / toolbar maximalism | The LLM is the command palette — discovery is a chat sentence, not a menu hunt. |
| Macro recorders / scripting-GUI builders | The LLM is the macro author; it writes `.script.py` directly. |
| Gumball / direct-modeling maximalism | Keep a basic gumball; the LLM edits the feature tree. |
| In-app wizards / tutorials / onboarding tours | The chat is the wizard — context-specific guidance on demand. |

---

## How to contribute

Pick a task from [`tasks.md`](./tasks.md) (sized for a single isolated agent run), or open an issue proposing a new long-tail sector line. The roadmap states *why* and *in what order*; `tasks.md` is the *how*. Keep them in sync: when a priority moves here, move the corresponding tasks there.
